Loading... setTimeout(()=>document.getElementById('_loading').classList.add('show'),0); if (location.href.startsWith('https://')) { window.versionsPromise = fetch('versions.json').then(r => r.json()); } var docgen_ondisplay = null; Symphony 2026.1 Administration Guide © 2026 Panzura 1 Overview 1.1 Introduction Panzura Symphony is a heterogeneous Data Management System. As well as providing data insights from file metadata, Symphony automates and manages tiering and data mobility between file systems, object stores and cloud storage services. Use cases include storage cost optimization, backup optimization and workload placement. In a tiering scenario, files are migrated from primary storage locations to secondary storage locations. Files are demigrated transparently when accessed by a user or application. Symphony also provides data mobility functionality to copy and move files, as well as a range of Disaster Recovery options. 1.2 System Components The diagram below provides an overview of a Symphony tiering deployment. All communication between Symphony components is secured with Transport Layer Security (TLS). The individual components are described below. Symphony System Overview Data insight and data mobility deployments will require fewer components. Symphony AdminCenter AdminCenter is the system's policy manager. It provides a centralized web-based configuration interface, and is responsible for task scheduling, server monitoring and file reporting. It lies outside the data path for file transfers. Symphony Agent Symphony Agent performs file operations as directed by AdminCenter Policies. The Agent is also responsible for retrieving tiered file data from secondary storage upon user / application access. File operations include migration, move, copy and demigration, as well as a range of operations to assist disaster recovery. Data is streamed directly between agents and storage without any intermediary staging on disk. When installed in a Gateway configuration, Symphony Agent does not allow tiering of files from that server, instead, the Agent provides access to third-party protocols and devices. Device specific configuration details (such as sensitive encryption keys and authentication details) are isolated from the file servers. Optionally, Gateways can be configured for High-Availability (HA). Symphony FPolicy Server FPolicy Server provides tiering support for NetApp filers via the NetApp FPolicy protocol. This component is the equivalent of Symphony Agent for NetApp filers. FPolicy Server may also be configured for High-Availability (HA). Symphony LinkConnect Server LinkConnect Server provides link-based tiering support for either Dell EMC OneFS or as an alternative method for migrating files from Windows Server volumes in the case where an agent may not be installed directly on the file server. This component performs a similar role to Symphony Agent for SMB shares. LinkConnect Server may also be configured for High-Availability (HA). Symphony DrTool Symphony DrTool is an additional application that assists in Disaster Recovery. 1.3 AdminCenter Concepts Symphony AdminCenter is the web-based interface that provides central management of a Symphony deployment. It is installed as part of the Admin Tools package. Upon logging in to the AdminCenter, the Dashboard will be displayed &ndash; we will come back to the dashboard in link . For now, the remainder of this section will follow the AdminCenter's navigation menu. 1.3.1 Servers The Servers page displays the installed and activated agents across the deployment of Symphony. Health information and statistics are provided for each server or cluster node. You will use this page when activating the other components in your system. Click a Server's ellipsis control to: view additional server information configure storage plugins add / retire / restart cluster nodes upgrade a standalone server to high-availability view detailed charts of recent activity edit server-specific configuration (see link ) 1.3.2 Sources Sources describe volumes or folders to which Policies may be applied (i.e., locations from which data may be transferred). Optionally, a Source may also specify a point-in-time at which to view a versioned object store, or a snapshot of a filesystem. A Source location is specified by a URI. Platform-specific information for all supported sources is detailed in link . A filesystem browser is provided to assist in setting the URI location interactively. Subdirectory Filtering Within a given Source, individual directory subtrees may be included or excluded to provide greater control over which files are eligible for policy operations. Excluded directories will not be traversed. On the Source Details page, the directory tree may be expanded and explored in the Subdirectory Filtering section. By default, the entire source will be included. 1.3.3 Destinations Destinations are storage locations that Policies may write files to. Platform-specific information for all supported destinations is detailed in link . Destinations are specified by entering a URI using the browser panel &ndash; if the specified folder does not exist, it will be created at Policy execution time. Optionally, a Destination may be configured to use Write Once Read Many (WORM) semantics for migration operations. This option is useful when the underlying storage device has WORM-like behavior, but is exposed using a generic protocol. 1.3.4 Rules Rules allow a specific subset of files within a Source or Sources to be selected for processing. Rules can match a variety of metadata: Filename / pathname Maximum path length File size Timestamps / age File owner File owner AD group membership Windows extended attributes Object storage (HTTP) user metadata Object storage class Attribute flags A rule matches if all of its specified criteria match the file's metadata. However, rules can be negated or compounded as necessary to perform more complex matches. You will be able to simulate your Rules against your Sources during Policy creation. Some criteria are specified as comma-separated lists of patterns: wildcard patterns, e.g. *.doc (see link ) regular expressions, e.g. /2004-06-[0-9][0-9]\.log/ (see link ) Note that: files match if any one of the patterns in the list match whitespace before and after each pattern is ignored patterns are case-insensitive by default (see link ) filename patterns starting with '/' match the path from the point specified by the Source URI filename patterns NOT starting with '/' match files in any subtree literal commas within a pattern must be escaped with a backslash 1.3.5 Policies A Policy specifies an operation to perform on a set of files. Depending on the type of operation, a Policy will specify Source(s) and/or Destination(s), and possibly Rules to limit the Policy to a subset of files. Each operation has different parameters, refer to link for a full reference. Optionally, most policies can be configured to log their results to an external database, in addition to the built-in textual logs &ndash; see here . 1.3.6 Tasks A Task selects one or more Policies for execution. While a Task is running, its status is displayed in the Running Tasks panel of the Dashboard. When Tasks finish they are moved to the Recent Tasks panel. Operation statistics are updated in real time as the task runs. Operations will automatically be executed in parallel, see link for more details. Launching Tasks While Tasks may be launched manually, it is often more desirable to enable a Task's schedule with a specific start time and optional repeat configuration. If multiple Tasks are scheduled to launch simultaneously, Policies on each Source are grouped such that only a single traversal of each file system is required. To launch a task using a webhook or the Management API, refer to link . Completion Notification When a Task finishes running, regardless of whether it succeeds or fails, a completion notification email may be sent as a convenience to the administrator. This notification email contains summary information similar to that available in the Recent Tasks panel on the Dashboard. To use this feature, either: check the Notify completion option when configuring the Task, or click the notify icon on a running task on the Dashboard Post-run Actions Each Task may be configured to perform one or more post-run actions. Use post-run actions to start further tasks, POST to remote HTTP servers to trigger 3rd party webhooks or start jobs within orchestration platforms (Ansible Tower, Puppet Enterprise, Control-M, Jenkins, etc), run local programs / scripts, or run remote commands via SSH. Each post-run action may be performed for one or more of the following Task outcomes: the Task is stopped by a user a fatal Policy error has occurred all Policies have completed but some operations failed all attempted operations were successful but locked files were skipped all operations were successful Note that when a Task spans multiple Sources &ndash; which will result in multiple corresponding entries in the Running / Recent Tasks lists &ndash; the outcome of the Task is the most severe of the above outcomes. For example, with two Sources, if all operations succeed on one Source, but the Policies on the other Source complete with errors, the outcome of the entire Task would be all Policies have completed but some operations failed . Post-run actions will be performed once the Task's Policies have been completed (or stopped) for all Sources. 1.3.7 DB Sources DB Sources, or Database Sources, are used as an alternative to Sources-and-Rules to select the files on which a Policy is to operate. Each result in a database query corresponds to a single file that the Policy should be applied to. Use a DB Source when the set of source files is either already known and is stored in an SQL database or MetadataHub repository, or when the set of files can be derived using other metadata held in such a database using a suitable query. For more information about SQL-based DB Sources, refer to here . MetadataHub DB Sources require a Knowledge Edition license. See here for more information. 1.3.8 Tag Queries In Knowledge Edition, Tag Queries are used by DB Sources to specify both the filters to be used for file selection, as well as any additional metadata tags that should be retrieved for use as parameters by other features (e.g. filename transformation in a Copy Policy). 1.3.9 Bulk Edit The Bulk Edit feature assists when creating, modifying or deleting a large number of Sources, Policies, etc at one time. Many items, together with the relationships between them, may be specified in a CSV file and then uploaded to be processed as a single bulk edit. Any errors will be reported so that they may be addressed before resubmitting the file. Download a CSV template from the Bulk Edit page to get started. CSV files can be edited using spreadsheet software such as Microsoft Excel, or easily be output from a script. Note that some advanced features may not be exposed via this interface. 1.3.10 Browser The built-in Browser enables examination of a variety of source / destination locations. Features include: Metadata display and sorting Optional filtering based on filename pattern or Rules Download, upload, and deletion of files For versioned object stores, files may be viewed at a specified a point-in-time For filesystems, files may viewed within a snapshot 1.3.11 Reports In addition to an interactive ACL Analysis report, Directory Usage breakdown, and general file, hardlink and symlink statistics, Reports (generated by Scan Policies) may contain charts detailing: a 30-day review of access and change activity a long-term trend chart to assist with planning tiering strategy a breakdown of the most common file types a breakdown of file ownership object storage class information (where supported) object storage user metadata Windows extended attributes Windows Alternate Data Stream (ADS) names Windows reparse points Reports may also include an exportable chargeback report enabling storage costs to be attributed to projects or departments within the organization. To generate an aggregate report across a number of Sources, configure a single Scan Policy to scan the whole set of Sources of interest. In this case, a report will be generated for each Source, together with an additional aggregate report covering the entire set of Sources. Secure links to reports may be shared with other members of your organization without the need to grant these users AdminCenter login access. Either share individual reports or share all reports generated by a Policy on an ongoing basis. To limit access to reports by IP address / subnet, refer to link . A configurable number of historical reports will be retained to record the results of multiple runs of each Scan Policy (see Settings → Report Retention). 1.3.12 Recovery The Recovery page provides access to multiple versions of the recovery files produced by each Create Recovery File From Source/Destination Policy. Retention options may be adjusted in Settings. Refer to link for more information on performing recovery operations. 1.3.13 Settings The AdminCenter Settings page allows configuration of a wide range of global settings including: email notification configuration backup (see link ) security roles (see link ) work hours AdminCenter logging and Syslog settings AD Global Catalog servers Additionally, it is possible to: view and update the product license suspend the scheduler to prevent scheduled Tasks launching while maintenance procedures are being performed update the TLS certificate for the AdminCenter web interface Server-specific settings and plugin configuration are available via the Servers page. 1.3.14 Help The Help page provides version information, as well as links to documentation and support resources. You may also view the global log, or generate a system diagnostic file ( support.zip ) for use when contacting Panzura Support. 1.4 AdminCenter Dashboard The Dashboard provides a concise view of the Symphony system status, current activity and recent task history. It may also be used to run Tasks on-demand via the Launch Task control. The Notices panel summarizes system issues that need to be addressed by the administrator. For instance, this panel will guide you through initial setup tasks such as license installation. The circular Servers display shows high-level health information for the servers / clusters in the Symphony deployment. Licensed quota consumption is shown on the Quota panel. 1.4.1 Storage Charts Primary and Secondary storage charts may be read together to gain insight into the impact of currently configured tiering policies on primary and secondary storage consumption over time. Each bar indicates an amount of storage space consumed or released. Consumed storage is indicated by a positive bar, while released storage is shown in the negative. Stacked bars indicate the contributions of the different operations by color. For instance, a Migration Policy consumes secondary storage in order to release primary storage. By contrast, demigration consumes primary storage immediately, but defers release until later. Specifically, either the primary storage is released by a Quick-Remigrate, or the associated secondary storage is released by a Scrub. In a complex environment, these charts provide insight into patterns of user-behavior and policy activity. Click on a bar to zoom in to an hourly breakdown for the chosen day. 1.4.2 Other Charts The Processed line chart graphs both the rate of operations successfully performed and data processed over time. Data transfer and bytes Quick-Remigrated (i.e. without any transfer required) are shown separately. The Operations breakdown chart shows successful activity by operation type across the whole system over time. Additionally, per-server operations charts are available via the Servers page &ndash; see link . The Operations radar chart shows a visual representation of the relative operation profile across your deployment. Two figures are drawn, one for each of the two preceding 7-day periods. This allows behavioral change from week to week to be seen at a glance. 1.4.3 Task Control & History A summary of progress is displayed for each running or recently completed Task. Multiple summaries will be displayed where a Task's Policies are configured to act upon multiple Sources. It is possible to stop Tasks, update task configuration, or request a completion notification for a task that is already in progress. Task summaries include any relevant status messages and warnings, as well as statistics such as number of files examined, operations succeeded, operations failed, locked files, etc. Note that these counts may not always simply add up to the number of files on the filesystem. For example, sometimes it may be necessary to re-examine files (leading to a higher number of files examined, although file operations will still only be performed once). Similarly, the number of operations succeeded may be greater than the number of files because multiple operations are being performed on each matching file or because operations are additionally being performed on directories. Per-file operation details (including any error messages) may be viewed by clicking a Task's log icon. 2 Deployment Refer to these instructions during initial deployment and when adding new components. For upgrade instructions, please refer to link instead. For further information about each supported storage platform, refer to link . 2.1 Prerequisites AD/LDAP Authentication It is strongly recommended that production deployments utilize Active Directory authentication via Secure LDAP. Prior to installing Symphony Admin Tools in this configuration: Obtain the FQDNs of two Active Directory domain controllers on your domain which are configured as Global Catalog servers Ensure that TCP port 3269 on both domain controllers will be reachable from the Admin Tools server (see also link ) Ensure that both domain controller LDAP servers are secured with a TLS certificate For example, on each server, install a TLS certificate, which must include the domain controller's FQDN in the Subject Alternative Name, in the Local Computer's Personal Store, along with the corresponding private key; restart the domain controller to detect the certificate Ensure that the Root CA certificate used to sign the domain controller TLS certificates is installed on the Symphony Admin Tools server in the Local Computer's Trusted Root Certification Authorities store Note that if a domain controller TLS certificate is not correctly installed, the LDAP server may still accept connections on port 3269 but that these connections will be immediately dropped by the server due to the incomplete TLS configuration. 2.2 Installing Symphony Admin Tools The Symphony Admin Tools package consists of the AdminCenter and the DrTool application. Admin Tools must be installed before any other components. System Requirements A dedicated server with a supported operating system: Windows Server 2025 Windows Server 2022 Windows Server 2019 Windows Server 2016 Minimum 12GB RAM (recommended 16GB+) Minimum 10GB disk space for log files Active clock synchronization (e.g. via NTP) Additional Memory Considerations If Duplicate Estimation reporting is required, allow an additional 100MB RAM and 6GB of disk space for each concurrent duplicate estimation. See also . Setup Run Panzura Symphony Admin Tools.exe Follow the instructions on screen 2.2.1 Initial Configuration After completing the installation process, Admin Tools must be configured via the AdminCenter web interface. The AdminCenter will be opened automatically and can be found later via the Start Menu. The web interface will lead you through the process of initial configuration: refer to the Notices panel on the Dashboard to ensure that all steps are completed. Consider configuring additional users or IP restrictions &ndash; see link . NFS Browser Agent If you are planning to use NFS storage, Symphony Gateway Agent should also be installed on the same server as Admin Tools. Remember to install this when installing other Agents. 2.3 Installing Agents Each Agent server may fulfill one of two roles, selected at installation time. In the Fileserver Agent for migration role, an agent assists the operating system to migrate and demigrate files (tiering). It is essential for the agent to be installed on all machines from which files will be migrated. By contrast, in the Gateway Agent role, an agent provides access to external devices and storage services. While it does allow access to local disk and mounted SAN volumes, it does not provide local migration source support. Storage plugins will normally be deployed on Gateways. 2.3.1 High-Availability Gateway Configuration When using Gateway Agents to access third-party devices or storage services using Symphony plugins or the smb scheme, a high-availability gateway configuration is recommended. Such Gateway Agents must be activated as 'High-Availability Gateway Agents'. Note: When using a Windows failover cluster to provide Gateway access to a mounted SAN volume, the server must be activated as a 'Windows Failover Cluster' rather than 'High-Availability Gateway Agent'. High-Availability Gateway DNS Setup At least two Gateway Agents are required for High-Availability. Add each Gateway Agent server to DNS Create an FQDN that resolves to all of the IP addresses Use this FQDN when activating the HA Servers Use this FQDN (or a CNAME alias to it) in Symphony Destination URIs For example: FQDN IP Address gw-1.example.com 192.168.0.1 gw-2.example.com 192.168.0.2 gw.example.com 192.168.0.1 192.168.0.2 Note: The servers that form the High-Availability Gateway cluster must NOT be members of a Windows failover cluster. 2.3.2 Symphony Agent for Windows Servers System Requirements Supported Windows Server operating system: Windows Server 2025 Windows Server 2022 Windows Server 2019 Windows Server 2016 Minimum 8GB RAM (recommended 16GB+) Minimum 2GB disk space for log files Active clock synchronization (e.g. via NTP) Note: When installed in the Gateway role, a dedicated server is required, unless it is to be co-located on the Admin Tools server in a small deployment or evaluation system. When co-locating, create separate DNS aliases to refer to the Gateway and the AdminCenter web interface. Setup Run the Panzura Symphony Agent.exe Follow the instructions to activate the agent via AdminCenter 2.3.3 Symphony Gateway Agent for Linux System Requirements A dedicated x86_64 server with a supported operating system: Red Hat Enterprise Linux (RHEL) 9 Ubuntu Server 22.04 LTS Minimum 8GB RAM (recommended 16GB+) Minimum 2GB disk space for log files Active clock synchronization (e.g. via NTP) Setup &ndash; RHEL In a root terminal: tar xzf Panzura_Symphony_Gateway_Agent_rhel9_2026_1.tgz Panzura_Symphony_Gateway_Agent_rhel9_2026_1/install.sh Follow the instructions to activate the agent via AdminCenter Setup &ndash; Ubuntu In a root terminal: tar xzf Panzura_Symphony_Gateway_Agent_ubuntu22_2026_1.tgz Panzura_Symphony_Gateway_Agent_ubuntu22_2026_1/install.sh Follow the instructions to activate the agent via AdminCenter 2.3.4 Symphony FPolicy Server for NetApp Filers A Symphony FPolicy Server provides tiering support for one or more NetApp Filers through the FPolicy protocol. This component is the equivalent of Symphony Agent for NetApp Filers. Typically FPolicy Servers are installed in a high-availability configuration. System Requirements A dedicated server with a supported operating system: Windows Server 2025 Windows Server 2022 Windows Server 2019 Windows Server 2016 Minimum 8GB RAM (recommended 16GB+) Minimum 2GB disk space for log files Active clock synchronization (e.g. via NTP) Setup Installation of the FPolicy Server software requires careful preparation of the NetApp Filer and the FPolicy Server machines. Instructions are provided in link . 2.3.5 Symphony LinkConnect Server A Symphony LinkConnect Server provides link-based tiering support for one or more Dell EMC OneFS or Windows SMB shares. This component performs a similar role to Symphony Agent without the need for software to be installed directly on the NAS or file server. System Requirements A dedicated server with a supported operating system: Windows Server 2025 Windows Server 2022 Windows Server 2019 Windows Server 2016 Minimum 2GB disk space for log files (on the system volume) Minimum 1TB disk space for LinkConnect Cache (as a single NTFS volume) RAM: 8GB base, plus : 4GB per TB of LinkConnect Cache 0.5GB per billion link-migrated files (Recommended minimum: 16GB) Active clock synchronization (e.g. via NTP) Setup Installation of the LinkConnect Server software requires careful configuration of both the NAS / file server and the LinkConnect Server machines. Instructions are provided in link for OneFS and link for Windows file servers. Other devices are not supported. 2.4 LinkConnect Client Deployment Installation Having deployed one or more LinkConnect Servers, all Windows clients that will need to access link-migrated files will require the LinkConnect Client Driver to be installed as follows: Ensure the client machine is joined to the Active Directory domain Run Panzura Symphony LinkConnect Client Driver.exe Follow the prompts Alternatively to ease deployment, the installer may be run in silent mode by specifying /S on the command line. This option is case-sensitive. Note that when upgrading the driver silently, the updated driver will not be loaded until the next reboot. Client Driver versions newer than the installed LinkConnect Server version should not be deployed. Deployment Considerations Access to NAS / file server shares containing files that have been link-migrated must use the domain credentials of the logged-in Windows desktop session. When a user accesses a link-migrated file, the client driver will transparently redirect the access to the LinkConnect Server if required. This redirected access will use the same logged-in Windows desktop session credentials. Installation of the client driver will enable remote symlink evaluation in Windows. If remote symlink evaluation was disabled prior to client driver installation, the driver will continue to prevent remote symlink access for other symlinks. Do not disable remote symlink evaluation (e.g. by group policy) after installation since doing so will cause the client driver to stop functioning. Client Driver Removal In the unlikely event that the LinkConnect client driver must be removed, please complete the following steps: Open an Administrator command prompt sc delete mwilcflt fsutil behavior set symlinkEvaluation R2R:0 Reboot 3 Usage 3.1 DNS Best Practice Storage locations in Panzura Symphony are referred to by URI. Relationships between files must be maintained over a long period of time. It is therefore advisable to take steps to ensure that the FQDNs used in these URIs are valid long-term, even as individual server roles are changed or consolidated. In a production deployment, always use Fully Qualified Domain Names (FQDNs) in preference to bare IP addresses. It is recommended to create DNS aliases for each logical storage role for each server. For example, use different DNS aliases when storing your finance department's data as opposed to your engineering department's data &ndash; even if they initially reside on the same server. 3.2 Getting Started 3.2.1 Analyze Volumes Once the software has been installed, the first step in any new Symphony deployment is to analyze the characteristics of the primary storage volumes. The following steps describe how to generate file statistics reports for each volume. In the AdminCenter web interface: Create Sources for each volume to analyze Create a Scan Policy and select all defined Sources Create a Task for the Scan Policy Launch the Task When the Task has finished, view the report(s) on the Reports page 3.2.2 Configure Tiering Using the information from the reports, create a rule to select files for migration. A typical rule might limit migrations to files modified more than six months ago. The reports' long-term trend charts will indicate the amount of data that will be migrated by a 'modified more than n months ago' rule &ndash; adjust the age cut-off as necessary to suit your filesystems. To avoid unnecessary migration of active files, be conservative with your first Migration Rule &ndash; it can be updated to migrate more recently modified files on subsequent runs. Once the Rule has been created: Create a secondary tier Destination to store your migrated data see link for platform-specific instructions Create a Migration Policy and add the Source(s), Rule and Destination Use the Simulate rule matching button to explore the effect of your rule Create a Task for the new Policy Launch the task When the task has completed, check the corresponding Recent Tasks entries on the Dashboard. Click on the log icon to review any errors in detail. Migration is typically performed periodically: configure a schedule on the Migration Task. 3.2.3 Next Steps link describes all Symphony Policy Operations in detail and will help you to get the most out of Symphony. The remainder of this chapter gives guidance on using Symphony in a production environment. 3.3 Configuration Backup This section describes how to backup Panzura Symphony configuration (for primary and secondary storage backup considerations, see link ). 3.3.1 Admin Tools Backing up the Symphony Admin Tools configuration will preserve policy configuration and server registrations as well as per-server settings and storage plugin configuration. Backup Process Configuration backup can be scheduled on the AdminCenter's Settings page. A default schedule is created at installation time to backup configuration once a week. Configuration backup files include: Policy configuration Server registrations Per-Server settings, including plugin configuration, credentials etc. Recovery files Settings from the AdminCenter Settings page Settings specified when Admin Tools was installed It is strongly recommended that these backup files are retrieved and stored securely as part of your overall backup plan. These backup files can be found at: C:\Program Files\Panzura Symphony\data\AdminCenter\configBackups Additionally, log files may be backed up from: C:\Program Files\Panzura Symphony\logs\AdminCenter\ C:\Program Files\Panzura Symphony\logs\drtool\ Restore Process Ensure that the server to be restored to has the same FQDN and IP address as the original server If present, uninstall Symphony Admin Tools Run the installer: Panzura Symphony Admin Tools.exe use the same version that was used to generate the backup file On the Installation Type page, select Restore from Backup Choose the backup zip file and follow the instructions Optionally, log files may be restored from server backups to: C:\Program Files\Panzura Symphony\logs\AdminCenter\ C:\Program Files\Panzura Symphony\logs\drtool\ Note: Restore from any backup (or virtual machine snapshot) that is more than 6 months old may fail due to certificate expiry. Contact Panzura Support for assistance if this occurs. 3.3.2 Per-Server Logs Backing up the configuration on each server is not necessary since such configuration is already included in the above Admin Tools backup process. You may optionally backup server logs from the logs location on each server &ndash; by default these are located at: Windows: C:\Program Files\Panzura Symphony\logs\Agent Linux: /var/opt/panzura/panzura-symphony-agent/log Note: Do not attempt to restore logs back into an active installation, since this will interfere with log rotation. 3.4 Storage Backup Each stub on a primary storage tier is associated with a corresponding MWI file on a secondary storage tier. During the normal process of migration and demigration the relationship between stub and MWI file is maintained. The recommendations below ensure that the consistency of this relationship is maintained even after files are restored from backup. 3.4.1 Backup Planning Ensure that the restoration of stubs is included as part of your backup & restore test regimen. When using Scrub policies, ensure the Scrub grace period is sufficient to cover the time from when a backup is taken to when the restore and Post-Restore Revalidate steps are completed (see below). It is strongly recommended to set the global minimum grace period accordingly to guard against the accidental creation of scrub policies with insufficient grace. This setting may be configured on the AdminCenter Settings page. It will NOT be possible to safely restore stubs or MigLinks from a backup set taken more than one grace period ago. Additional Planning To complement standard backup and recovery solutions, and to allow the widest range of recovery options, it is recommended to run a Create Recovery File From Source Policy after each migration. 3.4.2 Backup Process Perform these backup steps in the following order: Backup primary storage volumes Backup secondary volumes/devices (if necessary) Allow primary backup to complete first Secondary may be backed up less frequently than primary Usually, secondary backup will be run a little while after migration policies have completed Note: When adding backup jobs, always recheck the minimum grace period setting for scrub (see above). 3.4.3 Restore Process If primary and secondary volumes are to be restored: Click Settings → Scheduler → Suspend scheduler Restore the primary volume Restore the corresponding secondary volume from a newer backup set than the primary Run a Post-Restore Revalidate policy against the primary volume To ensure all stubs are revalidated, run this policy against the entire primary volume, NOT simply against the migration source folder This policy is not required when only WORM destinations are in use Click Settings → Scheduler → Start scheduler If only primary is to be restored (including where secondary is cloud storage): Click Settings → Scheduler → Suspend scheduler Restore the primary volume Run a Post-Restore Revalidate policy against the primary volume To ensure all stubs are revalidated, run this policy against the entire primary volume, NOT simply against the migration source folder This policy is not required when only WORM destinations are in use Click Settings → Scheduler → Start scheduler If restoring the primary volume to a different server (a server with a different FQDN), the following preparatory steps will also be required: On the Servers page, retire the old server (unless still in use for other volumes) Install Agent on the new server Update Sources as required to refer to the FQDN of the new server Perform the restore process as above 3.4.4 Platform-specific Considerations Windows Enterprise Windows backup software should respect Symphony stubs and back them up correctly without causing any unwanted demigrations. For some backup software, it may be necessary to refer to the software documentation for options regarding Offline files. When testing backup software configuration, test that backup of stubs does not cause unwanted demigration. Additional backup testing may be required if Stub Deletion Monitoring is required. Please refer to link for more details. NetApp Filers Please consult link regarding snapshot restore on NetApp Filers. 3.5 Production Readiness Checklist Backup Check your Symphony configuration is adequately backed up &ndash; see link Review the storage backup and restore procedures described in link Check backup software can backup stubs without triggering demigration Check backup software restores stubs and that they can be demigrated Schedule regular Create Recovery File From Source Policies on your migration sources &ndash; see link Antivirus Generally, antivirus software will not cause demigrations during normal file access. However, some antivirus software will demigrate files when performing scheduled file system scans. Prior to production deployment, always check that installed antivirus software does not cause unwanted demigrations. Some software may need to be configured to skip offline files in order to avoid these inappropriate demigrations. Consult the antivirus software documentation for further details. If the antivirus software cannot be configured to skip offline files during a scan, Symphony Agent may be configured to deny demigration rights to the antivirus software. Refer to link for more information. It may be necessary for some antivirus products to exempt the Symphony Agent process from real-time protection (scan-on-access). If the exclusion configuration requires the path of the executable to be specified, be sure to update the exclusion whenever Symphony is upgraded (since the path will change on upgrade). Other System-wide Applications Check for other applications that open all the files on the whole volume. Audit scheduled processes on file servers &ndash; if such processes cause unwanted demigration, it may be possible to block them (see link ). Additionally, check for other installed software that utilizes Windows File System Filter drivers. Test that the functionality of these products does not interfere with the demigration process or cause unwanted demigrations. The fltmc command can be used to determine installed Filter drivers. To see which drivers are registered on each volume, use the fltmc instances command. Monitoring and Notification To facilitate proactive monitoring, it is recommended to: Configure email notifications to monitor system health and Task activity Enable syslog &ndash; see link Platform Considerations For further information on platform-specific interoperability considerations, please refer to the appropriates sections of link . 3.6 Policy Tuning Periodically re-assess file distribution and access behavior: Run 'Scan' Policies Examine reports Examine Server statistics &ndash; see link For more detail, examine demigrates in file server agent.log files Consider: Are there unexpected peaks in demigration activity? Are there any file types that should not be migrated? Should different rules be applied to different file types? Is the Migration Policy migrating data that is regularly accessed? Are the Rules aggressive enough or too aggressive? What is the data growth rate on primary and secondary storage? Are there subtrees on the source file system that should be addressed by separate policies or excluded from the source entirely? 3.7 System Upgrade When a Symphony deployment is upgraded from a previous version, Admin Tools must always be upgraded first, followed by all Server components. Review provided release notes Verify that Operating System patches and updates have been installed on all servers in the Symphony deployment Run: Panzura Symphony Admin Tools.exe 3.7.1 Automated Server Upgrade Where possible, it is advisable to upgrade Server agents using the automated upgrade feature by clicking the upgrade system icon on the Servers page. The automated process transfers installers to each server and performs the upgrades in parallel to minimize downtime. If a server fails or is offline during the upgrade, manually upgrade it later. Once the automated upgrade procedure is finalized, the Servers page will update to display the health of the upgraded servers. Following the upgrade, resolve any warnings displayed on the Dashboard. 3.7.2 Manual Server Upgrade Follow the instructions appropriate for the platform of each server as described below. Agent for Windows Run Panzura Symphony Agent.exe and follow the instructions Resolve any warnings displayed on the Dashboard Gateway Agent for Linux (RHEL) In a root terminal: tar xzf Panzura_Symphony_Gateway_Agent_rhel9_2026_1.tgz Panzura_Symphony_Gateway_Agent_rhel9_2026_1/install.sh Resolve any warnings displayed on the Dashboard Gateway Agent for Linux (Ubuntu) In a root terminal: tar xzf Panzura_Symphony_Gateway_Agent_ubuntu22_2026_1.tgz Panzura_Symphony_Gateway_Agent_ubuntu22_2026_1/install.sh Resolve any warnings displayed on the Dashboard NetApp FPolicy Server Run Panzura Symphony NetApp FPolicy Server.exe and follow the instructions Resolve any warnings displayed on the Dashboard LinkConnect Server Run Panzura Symphony LinkConnect Server.exe and follow the instructions Resolve any warnings displayed on the Dashboard 4 Policy Operation Reference This chapter describes the various operations that may be performed on selected files by AdminCenter policies. 4.1 Metadata & Security 4.1.1 Scan Requires: Source(s) Generate report(s) for file sets at the selected Source(s). If desired, Rules may be used to specify a subset of files on which to report rather than the whole source. All reports include 30-day review, long term trend, tiering savings calculator and filetype breakdown. Additional reporting options are described in the table below. Feature Notes Analyze Windows ACLs See File Owner By default, owner statistics are omitted which generally results in faster policy execution. Chargeback by Owner Group Storage cost chargeback reporting based on file owner membership of specified Active Directory security groups. Prior to using this feature, configure AD Global Catalog servers on the Settings page to allow users and groups in all of your AD forests to be queried. Object Storage Archive State Include object storage archive state information (rather than only object storage class) where supported by the Source's object storage platform. Directory Usage Display an interactive usage breakdown of directories containing 0.1% or more of the scanned data. Potential Duplicates See link Metadata Export See Windows Extended Attributes Report on specified Windows extended attributes and export their contents. HTTP Metadata Report on specified object-store user metadata fields and export their contents. 4.1.2 Scan: ACL Analysis A Scan Policy may be configured to produce an interactive ACL analysis report for files and folders on Windows Servers or SMB-accessible volumes that do not simply inherit their access control lists from their parent folders. An ACL report allows the administrator to focus on relevant detail in the following ways: Only note-worthy entries are displayed &ndash; those files and folders that deviate from the their parents Details of each item's full security descriptor are shown clearly in one place, contrasted with the security descriptor of the containing folder Use-case specific filters can be applied to focus on the task at hand (such as auditing security, assessing accessibility or identifying ACL inheritance issues) Reports may be filtered to show only relevant items introduced since a previous report Note that some volumes may contain a very large number of files with explicit (non-inherited) Resource Attributes on files / folders that would otherwise not be reported. Since these attributes may significantly increase the size of the report, options are provided to omit Resource Attribute information where desired. SMB Gateway Agents may require additional configuration to include SACL support &ndash; see . 4.1.3 Scan: User Access Report When ACL analysis reporting is enabled in a Scan Policy, the resulting report may also be queried to produce an interactive User Access Report for a given Active Directory user which details the effective access granted to the user by file and folder DACLs. A User Access Report may also be exported to a CSV file for use with other tools. In the case of directories, computed rights are given for the directory itself as well as immediate child files, immediate child directories, other descendant files and other descendant directories. Entries are omitted where effectively covered by inheritance from an ancestor. To simplify the creation of third-party tools and scripts, CSV files are sorted in Unicode codepoint numerical order. Note: User Access Reporting may not be available for reports created on a older version of Symphony. 4.1.4 Scan: SID Search Report When ACL analysis reporting is enabled in a Scan Policy, the resulting report may also be queried to produce an interactive report of files and folders whose ACLs explicitly allow or deny rights to a given security principal. The security principal (user, group or computer) may be specified either by searching Active Directory or by providing the principal's SID directly. As well as showing rights granted, points in the directory tree at which the principal is denied rights are also clearly marked. In addition, the report shows points at which inheritance of such ACEs is either disabled (a protected DACL) or the normal chain of inheritance is broken. A SID Search Report may also be exported to a CSV file for use with other tools. Only non-inherited DACL ACEs mentioning the specified principal are recorded, except in the case of broken inheritance. Broken inheritance and disabled inheritance are flagged explicitly. To simplify the creation of third-party tools and scripts, CSV files are sorted in Unicode codepoint numerical order. Note: SID Search Reporting may not be available for reports created on a older version of Symphony. 4.1.5 Scan: Export Metadata Besides reporting, a Scan Policy may export per-file metadata for use by other tools. CSV / JSON Format File metadata, and optionally directory metadata, may be exported locally in either CSV or JSON format. Exports may optionally include ACLs &ndash; other metadata fields are included when the corresponding Scan Policy options are enabled. All export files are written to a policy-configurable location on the AdminCenter server, either uncompressed or in GZIP format. Export to Database Alternatively, this metadata may be exported to a database &ndash; see for more information. ACL Analysis The ACL Analysis option provides three exportable fields which describe the ACLs of the file or directory being processed, its parent directory, and the analysis result respectively. Each ACL analysis result consists of a string of zero or more characters where each character indicates a specific analysis flag as per the table below. Character Meaning W May widen access N May narrow access E Explicit DACL P Protected DACL (inheritance disabled) B Broken DACL inheritance F DACL no-auto-repair O Bad DACL ACE order Z NULL DACL (allows full access to everyone) Y Parent folder uses an auto-inherited DACL but this item does not a Audit ACE(s) present u ACE Audits NOTHING (missing success / fail flags) s Scoped Policy ACE(s) present l Mandatory Label ACE present L Multiple Mandatory Label ACEs present (warning) i Resource Attribute(s) present (inheritable) r Resource Attribute(s) present (item only) p Protected SACL (inheritance disabled) b Broken SACL inheritance f SACL no-auto-repair y Parent folder uses an auto-inherited SACL but this item does not C Conditional ACE(s) present G CREATOR OWNER or CREATOR GROUP SID specified without the INHERIT ONLY flag X ACE Applies to nothing (i.e. affects neither this item nor its children / descendants) d Owner differs from the containing directory D Group differs from the containing directory ? Unexpected ACE type - No analysis result was computed (this case is not the same as no characters at all which simply means that there was nothing note-worthy about this file or directory) When parsing this field, please note that since further flags may be added in future software versions, unexpected characters should be ignored. 4.1.6 Set Ownership Requires: Source(s), Rule(s) or DB Source(s) Set file and/or directory ownership to a specific AD security principal. A Set Ownership Policy will also apply to directories if the specified Rules also match the directory metadata. For the purposes of filename matching, directories match '.' or 'dirname/.'. A simple '*' rule will therefore match all files and directories. Note: if the file tree contains folders that specify ACEs in terms of 'CREATOR OWNER', any resulting effective ACEs will not be automatically updated to the new owner specified by this Policy. 4.1.7 MetadataHub Harvest Requires: MdH connection Perform a metadata harvest on a specified MetadataHub core or global search instance. Various MdH-specific configuration options can be provided including the directories to harvest, additional extractors, and file extensions to exclude. Progress of running harvests will be monitored during execution and displayed on the AdminCenter dashboard. As with other Tasks, post-run actions may be used to launch further Tasks or trigger external actions once a harvest has completed. This Policy is present only on Knowledge Edition installations. See also here . 4.1.8 Set Windows EA Requires: Source(s), Rule(s) or DB Source(s) Set or remove one or more Windows extended attributes (EAs). A Set Windows EA Policy will also apply to directories if the specified Rules also match the directory metadata. For the purposes of filename matching, directories match '.' or 'dirname/.'. A simple '*' rule will therefore match all files and directories. When used with a DB Source, the values of EAs to be written may be provided on a per-file basis from the corresponding database query. 4.1.9 Repair ACLs Requires: Source(s), Rule(s) or DB Source(s) Update Windows ACLs on Windows Servers or SMB-accessible volumes to repair broken ACL inheritance. DACLs and SACLs may be repaired either independently or at the same time. SMB Gateway Agents may require additional configuration to include SACL support &ndash; see . A Repair ACLs Policy will also apply to directories if the specified Rules also match the directory metadata. For the purposes of filename matching, directories match '.' or 'dirname/.'. A simple '*' rule will therefore match all files and directories. Some inheritance issues will not be automatically repaired by this policy. ACL analysis reports produced by the Scan policy will indicate if a particular instance of broken inheritance cannot be updated by the Repair ACLs policy. Reasons for this include: the ACL is not auto-inheriting; the original intent cannot be determined (e.g. ACEs in invalid order, more than one mandatory label); or an unexpected type of ACE is encountered. Please be aware that users and applications may be relying on the current values of ACLs in order to function correctly – it is recommended to use an ACL Analysis Scan first to understand the impact of this Policy and to take care to only target the appropriate area of the volume that requires repair. 4.2 Tiering 4.2.1 Migrate Requires: Source(s), Rule(s), Destination or DB Source(s), Destination Migrate file data from selected Source(s) to a Destination. Stub files remain at the Source location as placeholders until files are demigrated. File content will be transparently demigrated (returned to primary storage) when accessed by a user or application. Stub files retain the original logical size and file metadata. Files containing no data will not be migrated. Each Migrate operation will be logged as a Migrate, Remigrate, or Quick-Remigrate. A Remigrate is the same as a Migrate except it explicitly recognizes that a previous version of the file had been migrated in the past and that stored data pertaining to that previous version is no longer required and so is eligible for removal via a Scrub policy. A Quick-Remigrate occurs when a file has been demigrated and not modified. In this case it is not necessary to retransfer the data to secondary storage so the operation can be performed very quickly. Quick-remigration does not change the secondary storage location of the migrated data. Optionally: Quick-remigration of files demigrated within a specified number of days may be prevented &ndash; this option can be used to avoid quick-remigrations occurring in an overly aggressive fashion Policies may be configured to pause during the globally configured work hours Sparse files may be skipped &ndash; it is often undesirable to migrate files that are highly sparse since sparseness is not preserved by the migration process Alternatively, the Premigrate only option may be specified to transfer file data from selected Source(s) to a Destination in preparation for a later migration. With this option, files on primary storage will not be converted to stubs until a later normal Migrate or Quick-Remigrate Policy is run. Premigrate can assist if you have a requirement to delay the stubbing process until secondary storage backup or replication has occurred. Note: Premigration is intended to be followed by full migration / quick-remigration. If this is not done, a large number of files in the premigrated state may slow down further premigration policies, as the same files are rechecked each time. Migrates, Remigrates and Premigrates (but not Quick-Remigrates) consume license quota. For Sources using a LinkConnect Server, such as Dell EMC OneFS shares, see link instead. 4.2.2 Link-Migrate Requires: Source(s), Rule(s), Destination or DB Source(s), Destination For platforms that do not support standard stub-based tiering, Link-Migrate file data from selected Source(s) to a Destination. Files at the source location will be replaced with Symphony-encoded links (MigLinks) which allow client applications to transparently read data without returning files to primary storage. If an application attempts to modify a link, the file will be automatically returned to primary storage and then modified in-place. Files containing no data will be skipped by this policy. MigLinks present the original logical size and file metadata, however they do not retain alternate data streams or extended attributes. Since MigLinks remain links when read by client applications, there is no analogue of quick-remigration for link-migrate. Optionally: Policies may be configured to pause during the globally configured work hours Sparse files may be skipped &ndash; it is often undesirable to Link-Migrate files that are highly sparse since sparseness is not preserved by the migration process Link-Migrates consume licensed quota. 4.2.3 Demigrate Requires: Source(s), Rule(s) or DB Source(s) Return migrated file content back to files on the selected Source(s). Normally Demigrate policies are not needed since file content is returned transparently on user access anyway. Prior to running a Demigrate policy, be sure that there is sufficient primary storage available to accommodate the demigrated data. This operation may be used with both Migrated and Link-Migrated files. The following advanced options are provided: Disconnect files from destination &ndash; remove destination information from demigrated files (both files demigrated by this policy and files that have already been demigrated); it will no longer be possible to quick-remigrate these files A Destination Filter may be specified in order to demigrate / disconnect only files that were migrated to a particular destination 4.2.4 Quick-Remigrate Requires: Source(s), Rule(s) or DB Source(s) Quick-Remigrate demigrated files that do not require data transfer, enabling space to be reclaimed quickly. This operation acts only on files that have not been altered since the last migration. Optionally: Quick-remigration of files demigrated within a specified number of days may be prevented &ndash; this option can be used to avoid quick-remigrations occurring in an overly aggressive fashion Policies may be configured to pause during the globally configured work hours Licensed quota is not consumed. 4.2.5 Scrub Destination Requires: Destination (non-WORM) Removes unnecessary stored file content from a migration destination. This is a maintenance policy that should be scheduled regularly to reclaim space (and license quota). A grace period must be specified which is sufficient to cover the time from when a backup is taken to when the restore and corresponding Post-Restore Revalidate policy would complete. The grace period effectively delays the removal of data sufficiently to accommodate the effects of restoring primary storage from backup to an earlier state. Use of Scrub is usually desirable to maximize storage efficiency. In order to also maximize performance benefits from quick-remigration, it is advisable to schedule migration / quick-remigration policies more frequently than the grace period. To avoid interactions with Migration policies, Scrub tasks are automatically paused while migration-related tasks are in progress. Scrub policies may be configured to generate log output only, without actually removing files. If the Scrub feature is to be utilized, Scrub and Post-Restore Revalidate MUST be integrated into backup and restore procedures, see link . 4.2.6 Post-Restore Revalidate Requires: Source(s) Scan all stubs / MigLinks present on a given Source, revalidating the relationship between the stubs / MigLinks and the corresponding files on secondary storage. This operation is required following a restore from backup and should be performed on the root of the restored source volume. If only Write Once Read Many (WORM) destinations are in use, this policy is not required. This revalidation operation MUST be integrated into backup and restore procedures, see link . 4.2.7 Retarget Destination Requires: Source(s), Destination Filter, New Destination Permanently retarget stubs or MigLinks to a new migration destination. This operation is intended for use when completely decommissioning an old migration destination &ndash; the defunct copy of the file content will not be removed from the original destination either by this operation or by subsequent Scrub operations. Any old data that is no longer referenced by stubs or MigLinks will not be transferred to the new destination. This operation does not affect license quota. WARNING: This policy MUST be run on the root of all volumes that may contain stubs on all servers prior to finally decommissioning the old migration destination. Re-run the policies as necessary until there are no more files to retarget. This policy may be configured to pause during the globally configured work hours. 4.2.8 Change Destination Tier Requires: Source(s), Rule(s), Destination Filter, New Destination or DB Source(s), Destination Filter, New Destination Change the migration tier of selected files by copying the corresponding secondary storage data to the new Destination and then updating the stubs / MigLinks accordingly. The defunct copy on the original Destination will be removed by a subsequent Scrub Policy (scheduled separately and subject to the configured grace period). This operation is typically used to realize a multi-tier environment in which files can be aged across storage tiers over time. This is not to be confused with the Retarget Destination operation ( link ), which caters for the decommissioning of a secondary storage target. If desired, Rules can be used to apply different tiering criteria to different subsets of the data. Licensed quota usage will be transferred to the new destination files &ndash; scrubbing the original destination will not recover quota. This policy may be configured to pause during the globally configured work hours. Note: Files migrated to WORM destinations cannot be moved to another tier. These files will be skipped. 4.3 Data Mobility 4.3.1 Copy Requires: Source(s), Rule(s), Destination or DB Source(s), Destination Copy files from Source(s) to a filesystem Destination. For object store Destinations, see here . When a migrated stub or MigLink is copied, a full file (not a stub) will be created at the Copy Destination without demigrating at the Source. Path options: preserve &ndash; indicates that the relative path of each file, from the root of its source, should be preserved at the destination prepend server and volume name &ndash; prepends an extra directory component such as server_volname to the path copy full directory structure &ndash; copies all directories encountered when traversing a Source, even those that do not contain any files which match the specified Rules preserve directory metadata &ndash; preserves metadata for directories as well as files Metadata options: preserve timestamps &ndash; preserves time and date information preserve attribute flags &ndash; preserves flags such as 'Read-Only', 'Hidden', etc. preserve Unix ownership and permissions &ndash; preserves owner, group and permissions on NFS (this option must first be enabled on the Settings Page) preserve Windows extended attributes &ndash; preserves Windows extended attributes for all matched files (to preserve extended attributes on directories, also enable preserve directory metadata ) preserve alternate data streams &ndash; preserves alternate data streams Overwrite semantics: always &ndash; a file moved/copied from a Source will always overwrite any identically named file already existing at the corresponding location on the Destination never &ndash; never overwrites existing files at the destination rename &ndash; clashing filenames are disambiguated by renaming the new file. For example, if a file named letter.doc is copied to a Destination where a file with this name already exists, the new file would be renamed to letter[1].doc (or, if that too exists, letter[2].doc , and so forth) if newer &ndash; only overwrites the file if the Source file is newer than the Destination file The following are not copied: symbolic links, other reparse points. It should be noted that, where Source and Destination use radically different filesystems, some filenames may not be representable at the Destination and so will not be directly copyable. Similarly, Source filenames that are not considered unique by the Destination filesystem &ndash; e.g. differing only by case &ndash; will conflict with each other. Such conflicts may be addressed by using the rename overwrite option. Alternatively, Filename Transformations (see here ) may be applied to rewrite destination filenames and / or paths dynamically in order to accomplish a wide range of renaming and path restructuring operations. 4.3.2 Move Requires: Source(s), Rule(s), Destination or DB Source(s), Destination Move files from Source(s) to a filesystem Destination. If possible, the Move Operation will move migrated stubs without demigration, creating a stub at the Move Destination. A Move policy can optionally be configured to force demigration of stubs during transit if desired. Moving a link-migrated file always results in a full file move. Path, Metadata and Overwrite options, as well as Filename Transformations, can be specified in the same manner as for the Copy operation (see here ). The following are not copied: symbolic links, other reparse points. 4.3.3 Ingest Requires: Source(s), Rule(s), Destination or DB Source(s), Destination Ingest files into a cloud or object store Destination. Original filenames and paths are preserved. Optionally, original file metadata &ndash; and possibly a user-specified custom-metadata field &ndash; can be attached to the destination objects. The original files' security details can also be attached. Please see the relevant section of link for the specifics of how metadata is stored on a given destination. An Ingest policy must include a Collision Behavior option to specify the action to be taken when ingesting files that would overwrite existing objects at the destination. Supported behaviors are: Collision Behavior Description Overwrite existing file Overwrites objects unconditionally Always append timestamp Appends an ISO8601-compatible timestamp suffix to ALL object names, e.g. file.txt_20200401T115959Z Since partially ingested datasets are not typically useful, the policy will perform a configurable number of attempts to ingest each object. Such retries are appropriately logged for troubleshooting. Optionally, for data that will no longer be required on primary storage after ingestion, the original files may be deleted on a file-by-file basis as each file is successfully ingested. A Content-Disposition header can be automatically added to ingested HTTP objects such that user download via a browser will preserve the original filename (not including any appended timestamp suffix). Where security details are to be attached to ingested objects, the format is source-platform specific. For Windows files, a Security Descriptor (owner, group and ACLs) is recorded in Microsoft SDDL format for each object. For NFS sources, UID, GID and octal permissions are recorded as separate fields. An upper limit may be specified to prevent very large security details field values being attached to an object. Values exceeding this limit will be replaced with the supplied default value (or omitted entirely if a default is not provided). SDDL default values must be prepended with ' win: '. Filename Transformations (see here ) may be applied to rewrite destination filenames and / or paths dynamically in order to accomplish a wide range of renaming and path restructuring operations. A Scan policy may be used with a Rule that specifies maximum file path length to determine if the Source filesystem contains files with paths too long to be ingested into specific object store. 4.3.4 Restore S3 Archive Requires: Source(s), Rule(s) or DB Source(s) Enqueue S3 objects for temporary restoration from an archive storage class such as Glacier Flexible Retrieval or Glacier Deep Archive. Once restore requests are issued, this policy will wait for the object store to return all of the objects (which may take a significant amount of time). The performance of restoration operations can be selected, from the cheapest / slowest option (bulk restore), to the fastest / most expensive (expedited restore). The number of days that restored data will remain available must also be specified &ndash; if any objects are already restored or are currently being restored by other processes, this Policy will ensure that availability is extended if necessary to at least the specified number of days. After this period, objects will revert to their archived state. 4.3.5 Set Azure Access Tier Requires: Source(s), Rule(s) or DB Source(s) Set the storage tier of objects in Azure storage. Use this Policy to transition objects between 'Hot', 'Cool' and 'Archive' tiers. Any objects that are transitioned out of the 'Archive' tier will be processed asynchronously &ndash; this policy will wait for Azure to transition all of the objects (which may take a significant amount of time). The performance of archive retrieval operations can be specified, from the cheapest / slowest option, to the fastest / most expensive. 4.4 Delete Requires: Source(s), Rule(s) or DB Source(s) Delete files from Source(s). 4.5 Create Recovery File 4.5.1 From Source Requires: Source(s) Generate a disaster recovery file for Symphony DrTool by analyzing files at the selected Source(s). DrTool can use the generated file(s) to recover or update source files. Note: Recovery files generated from Source will account for renames. 4.5.2 From Destination Requires: Destination Generate a disaster recovery file for Symphony DrTool by analyzing files at the selected Destination without reference to the associated primary storage files. Note: Recovery files from Destination may not account for renames. It is strongly recommended to use Create Recovery File From Source in preference where possible. 4.6 Platform Transfer Requires: Source, Rule(s), Destination This operation is provided for professional services partners under special licensing. See also . 5 Source and Destination Reference The following pages describe the characteristics of the Sources and Destinations supported by Panzura Symphony. Planning, setup, usage and maintenance considerations are outlined for each storage platform. Read any relevant sections of this chapter prior to deploying Panzura Symphony in a production environment. 5.1 Microsoft Windows 5.1.1 Tiering Support Windows NTFS and ReFS volumes may be used as migration sources. To access files over SMB, see link . Symphony stub files can be identified by the 'O' (Offline) attribute in Explorer. Depending on the version of Windows, files with this flag may be displayed with an overlay icon. Windows volumes may also be used as Destinations. Note: If it is not possible to install the Symphony Agent directly on the file server, see link for an alternative solution using Link-Migration. 5.1.2 Planning When creating a production deployment plan, please refer to link . Cluster Support Clustered volumes managed by Windows failover clusters are supported. However, the Cluster Shared Volume (CSVFS) feature is NOT supported. As a result, when configuring a 'File Server' role in the Failover Cluster Manager, 'File Server for general use' is the only supported File Server Type. The 'Scale-Out File Server for application data' File Server Type is NOT supported. When using clustered volumes in Symphony URIs, ensure that the resource FQDN appropriate to the volume is specified rather than the FQDN of any individual node. 5.1.3 Setup See Installing Agent for Windows link 5.1.4 Interoperability This section describes Windows-specific considerations only and should be read in conjunction with link . Microsoft Storage Replica Symphony supports Microsoft Storage Replica. If Storage Replica is configured for asynchronous replication, a disaster failover effectively reverts the volume to a previous point in time. As such, this kind of failover is directly equivalent to a volume restore operation (albeit to a very recent state). As with any restore, a Post-Restore Revalidate Policy (see link ) should be run across the restored volume within the scrub grace period window. This will ensure correct operation of any future scrub policies by accounting for discrepancies between the demigration state of the files on the (failed) replication source volume and the replication destination volume. Integrate this process into your recovery procedures prior to production deployment of asynchronous storage replication. Microsoft DFS Namespaces (DFSN) DFSN is supported. Symphony Sources must be configured to access volumes on individual servers directly rather than through a DFS namespace. Users and applications may continue to access files and stubs via DFS namespaces as normal. Microsoft DFS Replication (DFSR) Agents must be installed (selecting the Fileserver Agent for migration role during installation) on EACH member server of a DFS Replication Group prior to running migration tasks on any of the group's Replication Folders. If adding a new member server to an existing Replication Group where Symphony is already in use, Agent must be installed on the new server first. When running policies on a Replicated Folder, sources should be defined such that each policy acts upon only one replica. DFSR will replicate the changes to the other members as usual. Read-only (one-way) replicated folders are NOT supported. However, read-only SMB shares can be used to prevent users from writing to a particular replica as an alternative. Due to the way DFSR is implemented, care should be taken to avoid writing to stub files that are being concurrently accessed from another replica. In the rare event that DFSR-replicated data is restored to a member from backup, ensure that DFSR services on all members are running and that replication is fully up-to-date (check for the DFSR 'finished initial replication' Windows Event Log message), then run a Post-Restore Revalidate Policy using the same source used for migration. Note: No additional licensed quota is consumed when stubs are replicated by DFSR. Retiring a DFSR Replica Retiring a replica effectively creates two independent copies of each stub, without updating secondary storage. To avoid any potential loss of data: Delete the contents of the retired replica (preferably by formatting the disk, or at least disable Stub Deletion Monitoring during the deletion) Run a Post-Restore Revalidate Policy on the remaining copy of the data If it is strictly necessary to keep both, now independent, copies of the data and stubs, then run a Post-Restore Revalidate Policy on both copies separately (not concurrently). Preseeding a DFSR Replicated Folder Using Robocopy The most common use of Robocopy with Symphony stubs is to preseed or stage initial synchronization. When performing such a preseeding operation: for new Replicated Folders, ensure that the 'Primary member' is set to be the original server, not the preseeded copy both servers must have Agent installed before preseeding add a "Process Exclusion" to Windows Defender for robocopy.exe (allow a while for the setting to take effect) on the source server, preseed by running robocopy with the /b flag (to copy stubs as-is to the new server) once preseeding is complete and replication is fully up-to-date (check for the DFSR 'finished initial replication' Windows Event Log message), it is recommended to run a Post-Restore Revalidate Policy on the original Symphony Source Note: If the process above is aborted, be sure to delete all preseeded files and stubs (preferably by formatting the disk, or at least disable Stub Deletion Monitoring during the deletion) and then run a Post-Restore Revalidate Policy on the original Symphony Source. Robocopy (Other Uses) Robocopy will, by default, demigrate stubs as they are copied. This is the same behavior as Explorer copy-paste, xcopy etc.. Robocopy with the /b flag (backup mode &ndash; must be performed as an administrator) will copy stubs as-is. Robocopy /b is not recommended. If stubs are copied in this fashion, the following must be considered: for a copy from one server to another, both servers must have Symphony Agent installed this operation is essentially a backup and restore in one step, and thus inappropriately duplicates stubs which are intended to be unique either disable all Scrub tasks during this process or ensure that Scrub Grace Periods are sufficient to cover the entire process, allowing for time that might be required in the event of any failures after the duplication, one copy of the stubs must be deleted immediately run a Post-Restore Revalidate policy on the remaining copy this process may render corresponding secondary storage files non-scrubbable, even after files are demigrated to prevent Windows Defender triggering demigrations when the stubs are accessed in this fashion: always run the robocopy from the source end (the file server with the stubs) add a "Process Exclusion" to Windows Defender for robocopy.exe (allow a while for the setting to take effect) test on a small set before performing a large robocopy job, then be sure to delete the resulting test copy immediately An enterprise backup solution may be used to perform a backup then restore instead of Robocopy /b. The advice above must still be followed , however, your backup process will generally have already been tested to confirm that it will not cause unwanted file demigration. Move Policies and Platform Transfer Policies provide alternative mechanisms to relocate files which have inbuilt support for handling of stubs. Windows Data Deduplication If a Windows source server is configured to use migration policies and Windows Data Deduplication, it should be noted that a given file can either be deduplicated or migrated, but not both at the same time. Symphony migration policies will automatically skip files that are already deduplicated. Similarly, Windows will skip Symphony stubs when deduplicating. When using both technologies, it is recommended to configure Data Deduplication and Migration based on file type such that the most efficacious strategy is chosen for each type of file. Copy and Ingest Policies are able to read deduplicated files as expected. Move and Ingest-with-delete Policies are not supported &ndash; perform the deletes as a separate step instead. Note: Microsoft's legacy Single Instance Storage (SIS) feature is not supported. Do not use SIS on the same server as Symphony Agent. Windows Shadow Copy Windows Shadow Copy &ndash; also known as Volume Snapshot Service (VSS) &ndash; allows previous versions of files to be restored, e.g. from Windows Explorer. Users cannot perform self-service restoration of stubs . However, an administrator may restore specific stubs or sets of stubs from snapshots by following the procedure outlined below. Be sure to provide this procedure to all administrators. In AdminCenter Browser, navigate to the relevant share using an smb:// URI Click point-in-time to select a snapshot Select the desired files, stubs and folders Click download For larger jobs, where a Policy is preferable, the point-in-time feature is also available when creating a Source. Encrypted Filesystem (EFS) EFS encrypted files are not supported. These files will be skipped by Migrate Policies. Bind Links Windows bind links (available in Windows Server 2025, first introduced in Windows 11 24H2) allow the binding of a file system namespace to a local 'virtual path' using the Bindlink API. While the use of regular bind links is supported by Symphony, the Merge bind link option is not supported due to outstanding deficiencies in the underlying implementation. 5.1.5 Behavioral Notes Symbolic Links Symbolic links (symlinks) will be skipped during traversal of the file system. This ensures that files are not seen &ndash; and thus acted upon &ndash; multiple times during a single execution of a given policy. If it is intended that a policy should apply to files within a directory referred to by a symbolic link, either ensure that the Source encompasses the real location at the link's destination, or specify the link itself as the Source. Mount Points / Junctions Mount Points are always traversed. By default all other directory junctions will be traversed as expected, unless the junction represents a legacy path, identifiable by its ACL explicitly denying the Everyone SID the List Folder permission. If it is desired to omit traversal of directory junctions, add the following setting to the Server's manual override settings in AdminCenter: Windows.TraverseNonVolumeJunctions=false Mount-DiskImage VHD and ISO images may be mounted as normal drives using the PowerShell Mount-DiskImage cmdlet. This functionality can also be accessed via the Explorer context menu for an image file. A known limitation of this cmdlet is that it does not permit sparse files to be mounted (see Microsoft KB2993573). Since migrated image files are always sparse, they must be demigrated prior to mounting. This can be achieved either by copying the file or by removing the sparse flag with the following command: fsutil sparse setflag file_name 0 5.1.6 Stub Deletion Monitoring On Windows, the Agent can monitor stub deletions to identify secondary storage files that are no longer referenced in order to maximize the usefulness of Scrub Policies. This feature extends not only to stubs that are directly deleted by the user, but also to other cases of stub file destruction such as overwriting a stub or renaming a different file over the top of a stub. This feature is not enabled by default &ndash; see here . 5.2 Microsoft Windows via LinkConnect Server 5.2.1 Tiering Support This section details the configuration of a Symphony LinkConnect Server to enable Link-Migration of files from Windows Server SMB shares. This option should be used when it is not possible to install Symphony Agent directly on the Windows file server in question. For other cases &ndash; where Agent can be installed on the server &ndash; please refer to link . Refer to link and link for details of the Migrate and Link-Migrate operations respectively. LinkConnect Servers pair Windows SMB shares with corresponding LinkConnect Cache Shares. Typically a top-level share on each Windows file server volume is mapped to a unique share (or subdivision) on a LinkConnect Server.
