A greater number of smaller migration destinations may be helpful in a recovery scenario where destinations can be recovered in order of priority. 5.18 Built-in NFS Client 5.18.1 Introduction Symphony Agents support NFS version 3 using a built-in NFS client. Both TCP and UDP connections are supported, but TCP is preferred by default. Files cannot be migrated from NFS sources. 5.18.2 Planning NFS servers must be configured to export file systems to the Symphony Agent servers. Typically, NFS servers only allow connections from clients that have been authorized by hostname. The NFS client accesses NFS servers using a UID of 0 (root) and GID of 1. It may be necessary to configure root squashing behavior accordingly, to allow UID 0 to access the files / folders of interest. See also link . An NFS share point at '/' is not supported. WORM Devices Some WORM storage devices present an NFS interface. If using such a device, be sure to set the WORM behavior flag on the Destination in AdminCenter. This will ensure that the agent expects the storage to exhibit this behavior. NetApp NFS Shares NetApp filers may not provide an export list to NFS clients via the usual mount protocol. To work around this limitation, NetApp NFS shares created for Symphony use must be created to export a top-level directory, e.g. /data . 5.18.3 Setup An NFS Browser agent must be installed on the Admin Tools machine to allow browsing of the file systems in the AdminCenter interface and Destination-based policies. Refer to link for installation instructions. 5.18.4 Behavioral Notes Symbolic Links Symbolic links (also known as symlinks or softlinks) will be skipped during traversal of an NFS file system. This ensures that files are not seen &ndash; and thus acted upon &ndash; multiple times during a single execution of a given policy. If it is intended that a policy should apply to files within a directory referred to by a symbolic link, either ensure that the Source encompasses the real location at the link's destination, or specify the link itself as the Source. 5.19 SMB Protocol Gateway 5.19.1 Introduction The smb:// scheme allows access to devices using the SMB protocol. Support for the smb:// scheme is provided by Windows Gateway Agents. No plugins are required. The Migrate operation is not supported for SMB sources. However, support for the Link-Migrate operation with both Dell EMC OneFS and Windows file servers via a Symphony LinkConnect Server is detailed in link and link respectively. 5.19.2 Panzura CloudFS Specific support for Panzura CloudFS shares is provided by the cfs:// scheme. It is recommended to use cfs:// to enable CloudFS optimizations and features. 5.19.3 Planning Prerequisites A Windows Symphony Gateway Agent (see link ), optionally configured for High-Availability Network For best performance, Gateway Agents should be placed close to SMB storage endpoints to minimize latency. 5.19.4 Setup Ensure the Symphony Gateway Agent is run as a dedicated user account that has full access to the SMB device(s) (see also link ). For a Windows fileserver, this means that the user should be a member of the fileserver's local Administrators group (it does not need to be a Domain Administrator). For Panzura CloudFS, the same applies: make the user a member of the Local Administrators group using the local-admin-add command in CloudFS Diagnostic Tools &ndash; see the Panzura knowledge base for more details. For other SMB devices, additional configuration may be required on the device to assign full privileges, backup permissions and / or 'root' permissions, depending on the vendor. If the Panzura Symphony Agent service user was not configured at installation time (that is, the service is running as 'Local System'), or if the user must be updated later, configure the Panzura Symphony Agent service: Open Services → Panzura Symphony Agent Stop the service Right-click and select Properties → Log On tab Check This Account and enter account name and password If the chosen account is NOT a local Administrator, it must be added to the Administrators group before continuing Note: it is recommended to specify the account in DOMAIN\username format Start the service 5.19.5 Usage URI Format (CloudFS) cfs://{gateway}/{host}/{share}/[{path}/] URI Format (generic) smb://{gateway}/{host}/{share}/[{path}/] Where: gateway &ndash; FQDN of Gateway Agent or LinkConnect Server host &ndash; SMB host server share &ndash; SMB share path &ndash; file system path, such as volume and folders Note: When accessing an SMB share on a device that is configured for Link-Migration, the FQDN of the corresponding LinkConnect Server must be provided. For shares on all other devices, provide the FQDN of any Windows Symphony Gateway Agent. Snapshot Support Where supported by the SMB host, snapshots may be selected in the Browser or Source editor. Policies run against Windows snapshot Sources will not traverse mount points out of the snapshot. 5.19.6 SACL Support Not all SACL features are supported on all devices. The SMB gateway agent must be configured to enable SACL features depending on which features are in use and/or supported by the particular SMB implementation: Navigate to the AdminCenter Servers page Click the '&#x22EF;' icon next to the SMB gateway server in question Click the Configure icon Select General → SMB SACL Support Update as required then Save and follow the instructions to restart the agent When transferring data between two SMB locations, in most cases, the same SMB gateway will be used for both Source and Destination. However, if different gateways are used, only SACL ACEs enabled on both gateways will be copied. 5.19.7 Additional SMB Credentials When a single user account cannot be used to access all SMB endpoints, or when an SMB endpoint requires credentials that are not a suitable user account with which to run the service, alternate credentials may be provided via the Windows Credential Manager. To add credentials via the Windows GUI: Login to the Windows desktop as the Panzura Symphony Agent service user Start → Credential Manager Add a Windows Credential Enter the SMB server FQDN as the network address Enter the username and password Restart the Panzura Symphony Agent service Alternatively, using the command prompt: runas /profile /user: DOMAIN\serviceUser DO NOT specify /noprofile since this will prevent the credentials from being stored persistently In the serviceUser command window: cmdkey /add: smb.server.fqdn /user: ALTDOMAIN\alternateUser /pass: password Restart the Panzura Symphony Agent service Azure Files Example When accessing Azure Files SMB shares, to obtain full administrative access, the Storage Account credentials should be provided rather than an EntraID login. runas /profile /user: DOMAIN\serviceUser In the serviceUser command window: cmdkey /add: storageAccount.file.core.windows.net /user:localhost\ storageAccount /pass: passwordKey Restart the Panzura Symphony Agent service Troubleshooting The Gateway Agent will log available credentials (excluding password) in messages.log on startup if available &ndash; search for 'Windows Stored Credentials'. 6 Disaster Recovery 6.1 Introduction The DrTool application allows for the recovery of stubs and MigLinks where normal backup and restore of primary storage has failed. Storage backup recommendations and considerations are covered in link . It is recommended to regularly run a Create Recovery File From Source Policy to generate an up-to-date list of source--destination mappings. DrTool is installed as part of Symphony Admin Tools. 6.2 Recovery Files Recovery files are normally generated by running Create Recovery File From Source Policies in AdminCenter. To open a file previously generated by AdminCenter: Open Symphony DrTool from the Start Menu Go to File → Open From AdminCenter... → Recovery File From Source Select a Recovery file to open Older versions of Recovery files may be found via the Recovery page in AdminCenter. 6.3 Filtering Results In DrTool, click Filter to filter results by source file properties. Filter options are described below. Note: When a Filter is applied, Save only saves the filtered results. Scheme Pattern In the Scheme Pattern field, use the name of the Scheme only (e.g. win , not win:// or win://servername ). This field may be left blank to return results for all schemes. This field matches against the scheme section of a URI: { scheme }://{servername}/[{path}] Server Pattern In the Server Pattern field, use the full server name or a wildcard expression. This field matches against the servername section of a URI: {scheme}://{ servername }/[{path}] Examples: server65.example.com &ndash; will match only the specified server *.finance.example.com &ndash; will match all servers in the 'finance' subdomain File Pattern The File Pattern field will match either filenames only (and search within all directories), or filenames qualified with directory paths in the same manner as filename patterns in AdminCenter Rules &ndash; see link . For the purposes of file pattern matching, the top-level directory is considered to be the top level of the entire URI path. This may be different to the top-level of the original Source URI. Using the Analyze Button Analyze assists in creating simple filters. Click Analyze Analyze will display a breakdown by scheme, server and file type Select a subset of the results by making a selection in each column Click Filter to create a filter based on the selection 6.4 Recovering Files Selected Files To recover files interactively: Select the results for which files will be recovered Click Edit → Recover File... All Files All files may be recovered either as a batch process using the command line (see link ) or interactively as follows: Click Edit → Recover All Files... Missing folders will be recreated as required to contain the recovered files. Recreated files and folders will not have ACLs applied to them so care should be taken when recreating in sensitive areas. 6.5 Recovering Files to a New Location When recovering to a new location, always use an up-to-date Recovery file generated by a Create Recovery File From Source Policy. To rewrite source file URIs to the new location, use the -csu command line option to update the prefix of each URI. Once these URI substitutions have been applied (and checked in the GUI) files may be recovered as previously outlined. The -csu option is further detailed in link . DO NOT create stubs in a new location and then continue to use the old location. To avoid incorrect reference counts, only one set of stubs should exist at any given time. 6.6 Updating Sources to Reflect Destination URI Change Generally, a Retarget Destination Policy &ndash; see link &ndash; is the most effective way to permanently move migrated data from one destination to another. If, however, the destination URI changes for some other reason, such as an FQDN being updated externally, DrTool may be used to repair the linkage between the source and the destination. In DrTool, source files may be updated to reflect a destination URI change through use of the -cmu command line option &ndash; detailed in link . To apply the destination URI substitution to existing files on the source, select Update All Source Files from the Edit menu. When given the option, elect to update substituted entries only. Note: This operation must always be performed using an up-to-date Recovery file generated by a Create Recovery File From Source Policy. 6.7 Using DrTool from the Command Line DO NOT create stubs in a new location and then continue to use the old location. To avoid incorrect reference counts, only one set of stubs should exist at any given time. DrTool commands must be executed from an Administrator command prompt. By default DrTool is located in: C:\Program Files\Panzura Symphony\AdminTools\drtool\ Interactive Usage DrTool [Recovery file] [extra options] Opens the DrTool in interactive (GUI) mode with the desired options and optionally opens a Recovery file. Batch Usage DrTool operation recovery file [ options ] Run the DrTool without a GUI to perform a batch operation on all entries in the input file. Note: The Recovery file provided as input is usually created by saving (possibly filtered) results to the hard disk from the interactive DrTool GUI. Basic Command Line Options operation &ndash; is either: -recoverFiles -updateSource if combined with -cmu , only matching entries will be updated -updateSourceAll all entries will be updated, even when -cmu is specified if operation is omitted, the GUI will be opened with any supplied options Recovery file &ndash; the file to open options (related to the operation are): -csu {from} {to} &ndash; to change Source URI prefix, this option can be specified multiple times -cmu {from} {to} &ndash; to change Migrated URI prefix, this option can be specified multiple times Examples All the following examples are run from the DrTool directory. DrTool -recoverFiles result.txt &ndash; recover all files from the result.txt file DrTool -updateSource result.txt -cmu nfs://oldfqdn/ nfs://newfqdn/ &ndash; update existing files to point to a new storage location DrTool -recoverFiles result.txt -csu win://old1/ win://new1/ -csu win://old2/ win://new2/ -cmu nfs://oldfqdn/ nfs://newfqdn/ &ndash; recover files to different servers and update the secondary storage location simultaneously Expert Options To use the expert options below, include -expert as the first parameter. WARNING: Restoring old ACLs into locations that may have changed significantly since the files were originally migrated can lead to unintended and unpredictable results. Use these options with caution. -do-not-restore-acls &ndash; this is the DEFAULT behavior (recreated files and folders will inherit Windows ACLs from the existing folders into which they are created) -merge-acls &ndash; restore files' explicit Windows ACLs and inherit from the parent folder -exact-acls &ndash; Windows ACLs will be restored exactly &ndash; if parent folder ACLs are now different, these will be propagated when a future change is made to the parent -restore-acls-disable-inherit &ndash; Windows ACLs will be restored, then inheritance will be disabled ( inherited central access policies and resource attributes will be discarded in favor of those inherited at the new destination) If -expert is specified when running via the GUI (rather than a batch operation), the GUI will prompt which of the above ACL options should be used. 6.8 Querying a Destination While it is strongly recommended to obtain Recovery files from a Create Recovery File From Source Policy, where this has been overlooked it is possible to obtain Recovery files from the destination. However, some changes in the source file system, such as renames and deletions, may not be reflected in these results. Querying the Destination from AdminCenter Run a Create Recovery File From Destination Policy, see link . A Pattern Matching Reference This appendix details the specifics of the pattern-matching syntax for filename and owner patterns used in Rules (see link ). For information regarding use of patterns in Filename Transformations, see also here . A.1 Wildcard Patterns The following wildcards are accepted: ? &ndash; matches one character (except '/') * &ndash; matches zero or more characters (except '/') ** &ndash; matches zero or more characters, including '/' &ndash; see also link /**/ &ndash; matches zero or more directory components Literal commas within a pattern must be escaped with a backslash. Examples of Supported Wildcard Patterns: * &ndash; all filenames *.doc &ndash; filenames ending with .doc (including '.doc') ?*.doc &ndash; filenames ending with .doc (excluding '.doc') *.do? &ndash; filenames matching *.doc, *.dot, *.dop, etc. but not e.g. *.docx ???.* &ndash; filenames beginning with any three characters, followed by a period, followed by any number of characters *\,* &ndash; filenames containing a comma Examples of Using * and ** in Wildcard Patterns: /*.doc &ndash; matches files ending with *.doc directly within the Source URI location, but not within its subdirectories public/* &ndash; matches all files directly within any directory named 'public' public/** &ndash; matches all files at any depth within any directory named 'public' public/**/*.pdf &ndash; matches all .pdf files at any depth within any directory named 'public' /home/*.archived/** &ndash; matches the contents of any directory ending with '.archived' directly within the home directory ( Source URI /home) /*/public/** &ndash; matches all files at any depth within any directory named 'public' where the public directory is exactly one level deep within the Source /*/**/public/** &ndash; matches all files at any depth with any directory named 'public' where the public directory is at least one level deep within the Source A.1.1 Directory Exclusion Patterns In most cases, directory inclusion and exclusion of specific directories is best performed using Subdirectory Filtering (see link ). For more complex cases, e.g. where directories to be excluded follow a pattern, create a Rule with the 'Negate entire Rule' box checked and enter a wildcard pattern ending with ' /** ' or ' /*** ' to exclude all files in trees matching the pattern. Directory exclusion performance considerations In some circumstances, ' /** ' directory exclusion patterns may avoid traversing the excluded subtrees entirely (resulting in fewer 'Files examined', similar to Subdirectory Filtering exclusions). However, while this mechanism is beneficial when excluding a large proportion of the full tree, it may be less efficient when excluding a smaller number of files. An alternative is the use a similar pattern ending with ' /*** ' which favors overall walk performance while still evaluating the entire tree. A.2 Regular Expressions More complex pattern matching can be achieved using regular expressions. Patterns in this format must be enclosed in a pair of '/' characters. e.g. /[a-z].*/ To assist with correctly matching file path components, the '/' character is only matched if used explicitly. Specifically: . does NOT match the '/' char the subpattern (?:.|/) is equivalent to the normal regex '.' (i.e. ALL characters) [^abc] does NOT match '/' (i.e. it behaves like [^/abc] ) Literal commas within a pattern must be escaped with a backslash. It is recommended to avoid regex matching where wildcard matching is sufficient to improve readability. Examples of Regular Expressions: /.*/ &ndash; all filenames /.*\.doc/ &ndash; filenames ending with .doc /~[w$].+/ &ndash; filenames beginning with ~w or ~$ followed by one or more chars /.*\.[0-9]{3}/ &ndash; filenames with an extension of three digits /public/.+\.html?/ &ndash; .htm and .html files directly within any 'public' directory /public/(?:.|/)*/ &ndash; equivalent to wildcard pattern public/** /public/((?:.|/)+/)*index.html/ &ndash; equivalent to public/**/index.html //home/.*/profile/ &ndash; files called profile in folders within Source URI /home A.3 Case Sensitivity By default, all patterns are matched case-insensitively using Unicode case-folding. Specifically, two characters are considered equal if they are the same or if they are equivalent in the Unicode case-folding table. This comparison is independent of language or locale settings. For example 'café', is considered equal to 'CAFÉ'. Of particular note is that Unicode case-folding will match lowercase 'i' with both the usual ASCII uppercase 'I' and the Turkish dotted-i ('İ'). To match using ASCII-only case-insensitivity (i.e. disable Unicode case-folding), prefix pattern with ' (?-u) '. To match case-sensitively, prefix pattern with ' (?-i) '. For a list of patterns, these prefixes must be applied to each individual pattern as appropriate. B Filename Transformations Some Policy operations, such as Copy, allow the use of user-specified Filename Transformations in order to rewrite Source filenames and / or paths prior to writing files to the Destination. Check the Perform filename transformation box on a Policy to get started. B.1 Transformation Steps & Execution A Filename Transformation configuration consists of a sequence of steps which will be processed for each file (and possibly directory) when the Policy is executed. The path of each file found in the Source (subject to the file matching the Policy Rules) will be matched against a regular expression (Regex pattern) specified in the first transformation step. If the path matches the pattern, it will be replaced as per the step's 'replace with' expression, then transformation will either: complete (no more steps will be executed) fail this file operation process a further step (e.g. Next step or skip to a specific step) If, however, the path does not match the pattern, the path will left unchanged and an alternative action (complete, fail or further step) will be taken. When execution of the steps completes, the resulting path will be used as the destination path for the file operation. File Paths Consider the example Source URI: win://svr.example.com/D/data/ A file within this Source, e.g.: win://svr.example.com/D/data/projectX/dir1/my%20file.txt would have the path: /projectX/dir1/my file.txt Note that this path always starts with a / and is not URL-encoded. Similarly, a directory path would have a trailing / , e.g.: /projectX/dir1/ B.2 Regex to Match Each step specifies a 'Regex to match'. This pattern describes the set of files (or directories) that this step will operate on and may also capture parts of the input path to be used when constructing the replacement path. As with patterns used in Rule matching: . does NOT match the / character the subpattern (?:.|/) is equivalent to the normal regex . (i.e. ALL characters) [^abc] does NOT match / (i.e. it behaves like [^/abc] ) a literal . must be escaped with a \ patterns are case-insensitive by default &ndash; see also here B.2.1 Absolute Regex Patterns An absolute pattern starts with a / character. Absolute patterns match the entire input path. For example: /projectX/dir1/.+\.txt &ndash; matches all *.txt files immediately within the folder Source /projectX/dir1/ /projectX/dir1/(.+)\.txt &ndash; as above, but captures the basename of the .txt file using () B.2.2 Relative Regex Patterns A relative pattern does not start with a / character. Relative patterns match one or more trailing path components. For example: .+\.txt &ndash; all *.txt files src/.+\.txt &ndash; all *.txt files within any src/ folder src/public/.+\.txt &ndash; all *.txt files within any src/public/ folder B.2.3 Directory Patterns Directory patterns end with a / character. Unlike a file pattern, a directory pattern will match all files and folders within a matching directory, enabling entire trees to be transformed (e.g. renamed or moved). For example: src/ &ndash; all src/ directories src/metadata/ &ndash; all metadata directories that are immediately within src/ directories logs_[0-9]+/ &ndash; all log directories like logs_123/ /home/(.*)/public/ &ndash; all Source /home/ User /public/ directories (capturing User ) B.3 Replace With Once a step's pattern has been matched, the input path will be transformed as described by the 'replace with' expression. A 'replace with' expression may be a fixed string, or may contain replacement parameters which represent, e.g. parts of the input path or various metadata values. For example (in Pattern → 'Replace with' format): (.+)\.htm → $1.html $1 expands to the characters matching the first capture group e.g. index.htm → index.html .+\.pdf → ${OWNER}/$0 ${OWNER} expands to the file's owner (e.g. John) $0 expands to the entire matching input e.g. File.pdf → John/File.pdf cases/CN([0-9]+)/(.+)_summary\.pdf → summaries/$1_$2.pdf e.g. cases/CN2974/jones_summary.pdf → summaries/2974_jones.pdf For a full list of replacement parameters, consult the table on the AdminCenter Policy page. B.3.1 Replacement & Directories When a Regex pattern ends with / , the matching directory tree will be renamed according to the replace with expression. For example: src/ → source/ &ndash; rename all src directories ([0-9]+)/ → $1_ &ndash; convert numbered directories to prefixes Generally speaking, the 'Replace with' expression should end with a / when renaming directories. Disregard Path Sometimes it is desirable to flatten a directory tree completely by simply discarding the path and put all files directly into the destination folder. This can be achieved using the following pattern and replacement: /(?:.|/)*/ → / B.3.2 Decision Steps Sometimes it is desirable to create a step that simply chooses between two different subsequent steps without changing the path. This is useful when there are several different lists of steps that are required, depending on the type of file. Decision steps can be used to select which list of steps should be applied to a given file. For example: .+\.html → $0 ($0 replaces the matching filename with itself &ndash; i.e. no change) B.4 Dry-run & Testing Before using a Filename Transformation on a production data set, it is recommended to test the steps interactively using the Test steps button on the Policy page. Additionally, it is recommended to run the Policy in dry-run mode in order to validate the configuration on the real data set without performing any actions on the files. Check the task logs to see the transformed destination URIs. C Network Ports The default ports required for Symphony operation are listed below. C.1 Admin Tools The following ports must be free before installing Admin Tools: 443 (AdminCenter web interface &ndash; configurable during installation) 8005 The following ports are used for outgoing connections: 4604-4609 (inclusive) 3269 (LDAPS authentication to Global Catalog servers) 443 (to contact the Global Licensing Service) Host: service.globalsoftwarelicensing.com Any firewall should be configured to allow incoming and outgoing communication on the above ports. C.2 Agent / FPolicy Server / LinkConnect Server The following ports must be free before installing Symphony server components: 4604-4609 (inclusive) Any firewall should be configured to allow incoming and outgoing communication on the above ports. NFS For each file server using Symphony Agent to connect to an NFS device, open TCP and UDP ports for the RPC Portmapper, Mount service and NFS service. Optionally, a Symphony Gateway Agent may be installed on the AdminCenter machine to facilitate browsing; this machine will then also require access to the above ports. The Portmapper always resides on port 111. The Mount and NFS ports however are registered with the Portmapper and may change when services are restarted. Please refer to firewall documentation regarding SUN RPC and the Portmapper as well as NFS service documentation for further details. The simplest solution is often to force the Mount and NFS services to use fixed port numbers. Other Ports Symphony plugins may require other ports to be opened in any firewalls to access storage devices / services from Gateway Agent machines. See also here . D AdminCenter Security Configuration D.1 Updating the AdminCenter TLS Certificate The AdminCenter TLS certificate may be updated via the AdminCenter Settings page by uploading a PKCS#12 certificate and private key pair. Alternatively, the certificate may be updated using the following procedure: Go to C:\Program Files\Panzura Symphony\AdminTools\ Run Update Webserver Certificate The new certificate MUST appropriately match the original AdminCenter FQDN specified at install time. D.2 Security Roles and IP Restrictions The Settings → Security Roles page allows for the configuration of multiple security roles to cater for different groups of users in Active Directory. Either full access or read-only access may be granted to an AD group, and access for each group may be limited by IP Address / Subnet. Webhook clients and Anonymous access for Secure Link Users &ndash; used to control access to shared links (e.g. statistics reports) &ndash; may also be restricted by IP Address / Subnet. If Active Directory integration was not configured at install time, you will still be able to restrict by IP Address / Subnet for the Administrator and Secure Link Users roles. D.3 Password Reset In a production deployment, AdminCenter is usually configured to use Active Directory LDAP authentication. In this case passwords should be changed via Active Directory as normal. However, if using local administration credentials, the password may be changed on the Settings page. Should the system administrator forget the username or password entirely, the credentials may be reset as follows: Go to C:\Program Files\Panzura Symphony\AdminTools\ Run Reset Web Password Follow the instructions to provide new credentials E API Access E.1 Webhooks Tasks may be launched from external applications using webhooks. Enable this option on a Task's Task Details page to generate a Task-specific HTTPS webhook URI. Since Symphony webhook URIs contain an authentication token, they must be kept secure to prevent unauthorized invocation. However, a webhook URI may be revoked at any time by either disabling the corresponding Task's webhook completely, or by regenerating the webhook URI (thereby revoking the previous URI's token). Access to webhooks may be restricted by IP Address / Subnet &ndash; see link . To launch a Task, simply send an empty HTTP POST to the Task's webhook URI. HTTP response status codes are given in the table below. Status Meaning 200 Task launched 403 The webhook is invalid or has been revoked 404 The Task no longer exists 500 Failed to launch: check Task configuration An entry will appear in Running Tasks on the Dashboard only for tasks that are successfully launched. If a second launch of the same Task is attempted immediately after a success, the second HTTP response will also be 200, but the Task will not actually be launched a second time (because the Task is already running). This avoids undesirable errors being reported when a webhook invocation is retried by the client due to a communications error. E.2 Management API If included in your license, most AdminCenter functions may be invoked via the EMA REST API. This API can be used to integrate Symphony with existing systems in the enterprise for automation, monitoring, statistics analysis and reporting. EMA authentication keys are created and revoked from the Settings page. Each key can be configured to provide FULL or READONLY access, and may be restricted by IP Address / Subnet as required. Given the capability of a Symphony system to access filesystems across multiple servers, care should be taken to ensure the security of these keys: Store API keys securely Restrict access to machines upon which client applications are installed (and their storage) Use READONLY API keys where possible Use a separate API key for each client application &ndash; this will allow them to be revoked separately if necessary Always revoke API keys for any applications that are no longer in use Use IP Address / Subnet restricted API keys The EMA development kit is included in the Symphony distribution package. E.3 Service Probe To remotely test whether the Panzura Symphony AdminCenter service is responding, perform an HTTP GET request on the following resource: https:// serverFQDN [: port ]/symphony/probe For example, to probe with curl: curl -i -k 'https://server.example.com/symphony/probe' The service will respond with 200 OK. F Knowledge Edition Symphony Knowledge Edition includes additional features to leverage actionable intelligence &ndash; such as file content derived metadata or externally tagged metadata &ndash; held in a GRAU DATA MetadataHub (MdH) repository. F.1 Setup F.1.1 Prerequisites The following are required to use Knowledge Edition features: A Symphony Knowledge Edition license One or more MdH installations Discuss the required MdH Core version with your Technical Account Manager MdH password(s) F.1.2 Configure Connections In AdminCenter Settings → Database Connections, add a new connection for each MdH Core or Global Search instance that you wish to query or harvest. In many cases, a Global Search connection is most appropriate. Use the 'Test' button to verify connectivity and authentication. Once configured successfully, connection status will be regularly monitored for each instance. Current status is shown on the AdminCenter dashboard. F.1.3 Harvest Metadata Metadata is inserted into an MdH repository by scanning filesystems of interest and recording metadata for each file using a selection of content-aware extractors. This metadata harvesting process can be orchestrated within Symphony by scheduling or launching a Task to run a Harvest Policy. See here . F.2 Usage F.2.1 Tag Queries Create a Tag Query object to specify a filter to select file entries of interest from the MdH repository. Multiple criteria can be combined as needed. Note that it is not necessary to specify the source filesystem or any directory path prefix in a Tag Query, this will be done in a DB Source. Optionally list any additional metadata tags that should be retrieved for use as parameters to other functions, such as Copy/Move filename transformations or Set Windows EA Policies. F.2.2 DB Sources Create a DB Source for use with one or more Policies. Specify a global search (or core) connection, filesystem location(s) and Tag Query. Use the Test button to confirm settings and check a sample of matching file URIs. Supported Storage Types The following storage types can be used with MetadataHub: Windows volumes, NetApp shares, LinkConnect shares, generic SMB shares, NFS exports, S3 buckets. F.2.3 Tiering Support Tiering Policies are supported for Windows, NetApp and LinkConnect. For Windows tiering, A Symphony Agent must be installed on each Windows Server that will require tiering support. When creating a DB Source, be sure to select the correct 'Type' rather than 'Generic SMB' to enable tiering. Note: In this configuration DB Sources will return 'winshare://' URIs rather than 'win://' URIs, this is required to describe file locations in terms of shares rather than drive-letter paths. F.2.4 Policy Limitations NFS and S3 Policy operations involving NFS or S3 DB Sources will not recheck that the current 'last modified' time of a file matches the MdH record prior to performing an operation. Specifically, in a volatile environment where files are re-written over time, harvested metadata in the MdH repository may be out of date &ndash; while Symphony will error if the last modified time has changed when processing a file on a Windows or SMB DB Source, for NFS and S3 locations the operation will be attempted anyway. G Database Integration Symphony can be integrated with various external SQL databases (such as Oracle Database, Microsoft SQL Server, PostgreSQL, MySQL, MariaDB, etc.) to allow both external selection of files on which to apply Policies, and to export Policy operation results and file metadata to external workflows. This functionality may used either instead of, or to complement, EMA API-based integrations. G.1 Database Connections Prior to using an external database, its JDBC driver must be installed and configured. To get started, navigate to Settings → Database Connections and follow the instructions to install the appropriate driver jar file. Once the driver is installed, add a connection. You will be required to provide a JDBC URL and any additional key-value configuration options. Read the sections below to ensure that you understand the configuration requirements for each integration use case. Once the connection has been configured, use the Test button in the Actions column to verify connectivity, authentication, etc. G.2 DB Sources A DB Source describes an SQL query which may be used as an alternative to Sources and Rules to select the files upon which a Policy is to operate. Each row of the result corresponds to a single file. Depending on the software that populated the database table(s), the file locations may be split across multiple fields (e.g. SMB server, directory path, filename, etc) or expressed as a single string such as a Windows file path. The DB Source editor provides a number of methods to easily map a set of result columns to a Symphony file URI. Escaping, '\' vs '/' conversions, etc, are handled automatically. Refer to the user interface for a full list of available mappings. Once a DB Source has been configured, it is recommended to use the Test settings button to ensure that the SQL query is valid and that results have been mapped to URIs as expected. G.2.1 Database-Specific Considerations As Policies are executed over a DB Source, the database query may remain open for a long time (because a large number of file operations are being performed). Additionally, the rate of consumption of query results may vary significantly throughout the run. Consequently, it is necessary to ensure that the JDBC driver is suitably configured to support this kind of streaming query. Specifically: The query must stream / 'batch' results &ndash; not return all results up front The query must not time out if results are not consumed for a while ClickHouse A ClickHouse driver (com.clickhouse.jdbc.Driver) is pre-installed. ClickHouse is recommended for its fast query performance. MySQL The MySQL Connector/J driver (com.mysql.cj.jdbc.Driver) provides two options for streaming. By default, Symphony will stream result sets row-by-row by specifying the MySQL-specific setFetchSize(Integer.MIN_VALUE) option. Alternatively, if the useCursorFetch driver option is enabled, cursor-based streaming will be used instead. This method uses more server-side resources since it creates a temporary table to back the query. MariaDB When using the MariaDB Connector/J driver (org.mariadb.jdbc.Driver), to prevent time out of connections when streaming, specify an option with key sessionVariables and value net_write_timeout=10800 . The timeout value is expressed in seconds and may be increased further as necessary. Oracle When using the Oracle JDBC Driver (oracle.jdbc.OracleDriver) to set binary Windows extended attributes, it is recommended to use the RAW , LONG RAW or BLOB data types &ndash; BFILE is currently not supported. G.2.2 Policy Behavior Generally, Policies will behave the same when processing regular Sources and DB Sources. The exception to this rule is that, during a Delete Policy on a DB Source, the size of deleted files will not be included in Server statistics (although the successful delete operation will be recorded). G.3 Output to Database G.3.1 Policy Logging Database logging is configured in a Policy by checking the Log to database option. This feature can be configured to perform one or more of the following: Perform a sequence of SQL statements, in a single transaction, before any files are processed (Pre-run SQL Statements) Log the results of individual Policy operations Perform a sequence of SQL statements, in a single transaction, after all file operations have been performed and logged (Post-run SQL Statements) A number of variables are available as parameters to the Pre- and Post-run SQL statements &ndash; refer to the help information within AdminCenter. G.3.2 Exporting File Metadata Scan Policies may be configured to export individual file metadata to a database table. G.3.3 Database-Specific Considerations When creating a table, choose column types carefully based on your database product and configuration. URIs, ACLS, error reasons and full error traces in particular may be very large, error fields may also be multi-line. Textual fields may contain Unicode. Numerical fields may contain 64-bit values. ClickHouse A ClickHouse driver (com.clickhouse.jdbc.Driver) is pre-installed. ClickHouse is recommended for its fast query performance. AdminCenter makes ClickHouse-specific CREATE TABLE recommendations for ClickHouse databases. These table specifications use the DateTime64 type to store file metadata timestamps &ndash; ensure that the ClickHouse date_time_input_format option is set to best_effort in order to parse timestamps correctly. For example, in /etc/clickhouse-server/users.xml: <clickhouse> <profiles> <default> <date_time_input_format>best_effort</date_time_input_format> </default> ... Microsoft SQL Server Typically, the NVARCHAR type should be used in preference to VARCHAR for Unicode support. It is recommended to add the useBulkCopyForBatchInsert=true driver option and increase Inserts per transaction to 10,000 . MySQL When using the MySQL Connector/J driver (com.mysql.cj.jdbc.Driver), it is strongly recommended to add the rewriteBatchedStatements=true for improved performance. Optionally, increasing Inserts per transaction to 10,000 may improve performance. The CSV engine is generally not suitable for logging since some fields may be NULL (depending on the particular operation result being logged), and NULLs are not allowed by this engine. MariaDB When using the MariaDB Connector/J driver (org.mariadb.jdbc.Driver), a modest performance improvement may be obtained by using the rewriteBatchedStatements=true option. Optionally, increasing Inserts per transaction to 10,000 may slightly improve performance. Do not increase any higher. Postgres When using the PostgreSQL JDBC Driver (pgJDBC &ndash; org.postgresql.Driver), it is recommended to add the reWriteBatchedInserts=true driver option and increase Inserts per transaction to 10,000 . Oracle When using the Oracle JDBC Driver (oracle.jdbc.OracleDriver), it is recommended to increase Inserts per transaction to 10,000 . Snowflake It is strongly recommended to increase Inserts per transaction to 100,000 . Note that if you intend to output to Snowflake using multiple Policies concurrently, this setting will consume a lot of memory (see below). G.3.4 Memory Provisioning Database output operations may consume significant memory, especially when running multiple Policies in parallel and increasing Inserts per transaction to very large values. Check task logs for 'memory performance score' &ndash; if the percentage is significantly below 100%, contact Panzura Support for advice. H Duplicate Estimation Scan Policies may be configured to estimate the degree of file duplication within a dataset to inform further storage policy or technology decisions. Depending on the nature of the decisions to be made, duplicate estimation may be performed either on a per-Source basis, or aggregated across a set of Sources. H.1 Estimation Method The number and total size of duplicated files is estimated by considering any file that has the same or equivalent filename and size as a previous scanned file to be a duplicate. File content is not examined for performance reasons. AdminCenter will require significant additional memory and disk space when using this feature (unless the Export hash only option is selected). Allow 100MB RAM and 6GB of disk space on the AdminCenter installation volume for each concurrent duplicate estimation. Concurrent estimations occur when either running multiple Scan Policies at the same time, or when a single Scan Policy produces estimates for multiple Sources without the Estimate over aggregated scope option. For large Sources, estimates will be computed by dynamically sampling files across each Source. H.2 Copy Templates In some situations, such as when a user makes a copy of a file in the same directory as the original, identical copies are systematically renamed to avoid the name clash. One example of this is the Windows Copy Name Template which, for example, might rename a second copy of 'file.txt' to 'file - Copy.txt' and a subsequent copy to 'file - Copy (2).txt', etc. For duplicate estimation, it is usually desirable to equate copied filenames by accounting for any such copy templates in use. Zero or more templates (i.e. patterns) can be specified in each Scan Policy as required. Example Templates: %s - Copy Copy of %s Operation Any file with a basename (i.e. the filename not including the extension) matching a template will be considered equivalent to just the part matching %s plus any extension. In addition, if a template matches, any trailing number of the form ' (n) ', ' (n) ', ' (nn) ' or ' (nn) ' will also be ignored. A template of just %s will allow all such trailing number sequences to be ignored. H.3 File Size Filtering Duplicate estimation can be configured to ignore files smaller than a particular size. This setting is useful because very small files with the same name that are not, in fact, duplicates are likely to look like duplicates and give a false positive. For example, a small metadata file that is present in each project with a fixed name, while different for each project, would have one of a small set of possible file sizes. This means that for a large number of projects with unique metadata, there is still likely to be number of false positive duplicate detections. Set this value to zero to include all files. H.4 Other Metadata In some cases, it may be desirable to match additional metadata, rather than just filename and size, before considering files to be duplicates. Options are provided for created, modified, ingest-created, and ingest-modified timestamps, as well as file ownership. H.5 Duplicate Detection Metadata Hashes Duplicate Detection Metadata Hashes may be included when exporting Scan Policy results to JSON, CSV or external Databases. This feature allows external processes to identify and act upon likely duplicates by matching the metadata hashes between files. The Export hash only option may be used to suppress inclusion of the duplicate estimate in the generated report, but still allow the duplicate detection metadata hash field to be included in exported file metadata. This option avoids the use of additional memory to perform the estimation. I Advanced Agent Configuration Agents may be configured on a per-server basis via the AdminCenter Servers page. When the configuration options are saved, they are pushed to the target server to be loaded on the next service restart. In the case of a cluster, all nodes will receive the same updated configuration. I.1 Logging Log location and rotation options may be adjusted if required. Debug mode may impact performance and should only be enabled following advice from Panzura Support. Additionally Symphony can be configured to send UDP syslog messages in either RFC5424 or RFC3164 format. Syslog output is not enabled by default. I.2 Stub Deletion Monitoring As described in , on Windows file systems, Symphony can monitor stub deletion events in order to make corresponding secondary storage files eligible for removal using Scrub Policies. This feature is not enabled by default. It must be enabled on a per-volume basis either by specifying volume GUIDs (preferred) or drive letters. Volume GUIDs may be determined by running the Windows mountvol command or Powershell Get-WmiObject -Class win32_volume . For Windows clustered volumes, the cluster volume must be specified using a volume GUID. Note: This feature should not be configured to monitor events on backup destination volumes. In particular, some basic backup tools such as Windows Server Backup copy individual files to VHDX backup volumes in a manner which is not supported and so such volumes must not be configured for Stub Deletion Monitoring. Of course, deletions may still be monitored on source data volumes. I.3 Parallelization Tuning When a Policy is executed on a Source, operations will automatically be executed in parallel. Parallelization parameters may be tuned for each Server if necessary. Adjust 'Max Slots' and 'Worker Thread Count' to control the number of policy operations (e.g. file migrations) that will execute in parallel. Adjust 'Metadata Worker Thread Count' to control the total number of metadata operations that may be performed in parallel across all SMB filesystem traversals on the given Agent. Before increasing this value, it is advisable to minimize the latency between the Agent and the SMB endpoint(s). I.4 NFS Client By default, the built-in NFS client accesses NFS servers using a UID of 0 (root) and GID of 1. Wherever possible, NFS exports should be configured to allow such access, rather than reconfiguring the client. All NFS settings will apply to all NFS connections from the given agent. I.5 Deny Demigrations Applications may be denied the right to demigrate stubs. Such an application &ndash; specified either by application binary name or full path &ndash; will be unable to access a stub and demigrate the file contents (an error will be returned to the application instead). Note: Only local applications (applications running directly on the file server) may be blocked. I.6 Enabled / Available Plugins Storage plugins may be configured and enabled as necessary for each server. For plugin-specific details, refer to the appropriate section of link . I.7 Manual Overrides Additional options may be manually entered. Undocumented options should not be entered unless under the direction of a Symphony support engineer. Unknown Content-Encoding behavior By default, an UNEXPECTED_CONTENT_ENCODING error is returned if an attempt is made to copy a file from an object storage Source where the source file has a non-identity Content-Encoding. This restriction avoids copying encoded data between systems in a way that will cause confusion at the destination. To override this behavior, and instead copy the raw bytes as encoded , specify a Manual Override: Azure: azure.dca.passthroughUnknownContentEncoding=true GCP: google.dca.passthroughUnknownContentEncoding=true AWS S3: s3.passthroughUnknownContentEncoding=true S3 Generic: s3generic.passthroughUnknownContentEncoding=true Cloudian S3: s3cloudian.passthroughUnknownContentEncoding=true Dell EMC ECS S3: s3ecs.passthroughUnknownContentEncoding=true IBM COS S3: s3bluemix.passthroughUnknownContentEncoding=true Wasabi S3: s3wasabi.passthroughUnknownContentEncoding=true DataCore Swarm S3: s3swarm.passthroughUnknownContentEncoding=true I.8 Upload Configuration Under some circumstances it may be necessary to upload a configuration file under the direction of a Symphony support engineer. The configuration for this server will be REPLACED in its entirety. J Platform Transfer Guide This appendix details the usage of Symphony's Platform Transfer Policy to facilitate the copying of large datasets between different filesystems and cloud storage platforms, including file and directory ACLs. Platform Transfer provides the detailed logging, retry and resumability capabilities necessary to support very large jobs run over the internet or other wide area networks. J.1 Cloud Object Storage In addition to fileservers and NAS devices, Platform Transfer is supported for cloud object storage sources / destinations on Azure (excluding ADLS), AWS S3 and GCP. ACLs from filesystems may be stored in cloud objects' metadata (subject to cloud implementation size restrictions) to be later restored to a filesystem by another Platform Transfer. Captured metadata may be browsed via the AdminCenter's built-in file browser. J.2 Planning Prerequisites A Symphony license that supports the Platform Transfer feature. Windows Scheme Selection As with other Policies, transferring data to and from Windows servers may be performed via the win:// scheme by installing Symphony Agent on each server. This scheme automatically supports all SACL features. However, to use a VSS snapshot as a Source, use the smb:// scheme and click the Point-in-Time button in the Source browser immediately after entering the URI in order to select the desired snapshot. Unicode Support For NetApp Filer destinations, it is recommended to set the volume language to utf8mb4 to permit the transfer of files with names containing Unicode supplementary characters. Configuring SACL Support When using SMB Sources and Destinations, not all SACL ACE types are supported on all devices. The SMB gateway agent must be configured to enable SACL features depending on which features are in use and/or supported by the particular SMB implementation. For SMB Gateways, refer to link ; for LinkConnect Servers, refer to link . When transferring data between two SMB locations, in most cases, the same SMB gateway will be used for both Source and Destination. However, if different gateways are used, only SACL ACEs enabled on both gateways will be copied. For more information regarding Dynamic Access Control and SACLs on NetApp, see also . Always check SACL configuration is correct before commencing Platform Transfer. J.3 Setup a Transfer In AdminCenter: Create a Source representing the location from which data is to be copied To avoid inconsistent results, transfer from a source that it not currently being modified by users (or a read-only snapshot which can be accessed using the smb:// or netapp:// schemes in conjunction with the Point-in-Time button) &ndash; to transfer an actively changing dataset, refer to Create a Destination representing the location to which data is to be copied For Platform Transfer to a non -cloud destination, the directory must be created upfront and its ACL must be set appropriately – generally, this means that the ACL should be the same as the ACL on the source directory (although the ACEs may be inherited from different parent folders) Ensure that the directory's SACLs are also set appropriately – depending on the site, this may include any or all of Audit, Mandatory Integrity Label, Content Access Policy and Resource Attribute settings If using Content Access Policies and/or Resource Attributes, make sure the destination server has the appropriate Group Policy deployed Create a Rule Typically, this will simply have a file pattern of '*' to match all files Create a Policy Select 'Platform Transfer' as the Operation Select 'Single-pass' transfer mode Generally, 'Number of attempts' can be left at the default value (3) To copy full file content, DO NOT check 'Duplicate migration state' (see ) Specify the Source, Rule and Destination created above If transferring data to a cloud destination, you may optionally specify a Storage Class Create a Task Select the Policy created above Save the Task Launch the Task J.4 Checking Task Results Running Tasks can be monitored on the AdminCenter Dashboard. Once a Task is completed, check its status in the Recent Tasks panel. Open the tile for a status summary and click the log icon to review per-file information. Although individual file operations will be retried several times on failure during the run to address minor transient issues, at the end of the Task run it is possible that there will still be outstanding file operation failures or that the entire Policy may have been aborted due to an insurmountable error condition. If such errors occur, simply re-run the Task (possibly after resolving any systematic issues in your environment). Each Task run will retry any previous outstanding file operations and resume the filesystem traversal from where the previous run stopped. Always re-run the Task until it completes successfully. Once fully complete, the Policy may not be re-used – create another Policy to transfer another dataset. J.4.1 Skipping a Directory for a Subsequent Run If errors occur for a specific directory that cannot be otherwise addressed, you may wish to exclude it from future runs. Do this by editing the Source and specifying an exclusion in the 'Subdirectory filtering' control. Note that once the Task has been started for the first time, you may not change the Source or make any Subdirectory filtering changes except for adding exclusions . J.5 Single-pass Transfer Mode Single-pass transfer mode is available across the widest range of source and destination filesystems and object storage. It is designed for use with unchanging filesystems or filesystem snapshots. The Source filesystem will be traversed only once. If aborted, a Single-pass Platform Transfer Task may be re-launched to continue from the previous termination point and retry outstanding failures. Once finally completed, further runs will do nothing. Directory Modification Times When each file is copied in Single-pass transfer mode, the creation of the file causes the parent directory's modification time to be updated. This results in different directory modification times on the Destination and Source by the time that the Task has completed. In the rare case that this is not acceptable, the modification times may be corrected later by creating a second Platform Transfer Policy that uses the same Source and Destination but a Rule that matches NO files. The directory metadata will then be re-copied. A Rule to match no files can be created using the following regex filename pattern: /^$/ Note that this second pass will not be required when using a cloud object storage destination. J.6 Multi-pass with Delta Synchronization Multi-pass transfers are intended for use with live filesystems that are actively being modified &ndash; specifically, they cater for the case where a large transfer would take too much time for it to be scheduled in planned downtime. Each run attempts to perform a complete 'pass', that is, it traverses the filesystem once, copying data as necessary. After the first run &ndash; which one might expect to take significant time &ndash; subsequent runs should grow progressively shorter as fewer outstanding changes need to be copied to the destination. This process is called delta synchronization. After a small number of passes, the delta should be sufficiently small that a final run can be completed in a relatively short downtime window prior to switching user access to the new filesystem. If aborted, a Multi-pass Platform Transfer Task may be re-launched to continue from the previous termination point. Once the entire Source has been processed (that is, a 'pass' has been completed), the next run will restart the scan to retry outstanding failures and to synchronize any changes on the Source filesystem. Multi-pass transfer may only be used with Sources and Destinations on Windows Servers or SMB-accessible volumes. Multi-pass transfer mode requires additional disk space on the AdminCenter server to record compressed delta synchronization metadata. Actual disk space required varies depending on path depths, filenames, etc, however it is recommended to provision at least 1GB of additional space for every 10 million files in your dataset. J.7 Migrated and Link-Migrated Files If the source filesystem contains Symphony stubs or MigLinks, by default the actual file content will be retrieved during the transfer operation. Specifically, the source stubs / MigLinks will remain unchanged and the destination files will be normal (non-migrated) files. If, however, you wish perform a Platform Transfer in order to &quot;move&quot; a migrated or link-migrated dataset from one platform to another, it will be necessary to check the 'Duplicate migration state' box in the Policy settings. When this option is selected, for each stub or MigLink found in the source dataset, a corresponding stub will be created at the destination. Note that this option is not supported for destination filesystems that use MigLinks. WARNING: The 'Duplicate migration state' operation is potentially dangerous since incorrect use may lead to migrated file content being prematurely removed by subsequent Scrub policies. Always observe the precautions below. Before performing the Platform Transfer: Disable Migrate, Quick Remigrate and Link-Migrate Tasks for the Source location Disable Stub Deletion Monitoring ( ) / Link Deletion Monitoring ( ) on the source agent Disable Stub Deletion Monitoring on the destination agent Disable ALL Scrub Tasks After the Platform Transfer has successfully completed (including any re-runs), the following steps must be performed, strictly in the order presented: DELETE the data from the source filesystem (so that only the files and stubs at the destination remain) Run a Post-Restore Revalidate policy at the destination – this will check that files' migration-related metadata is up-to-date Re-enable Scrub tasks as required Re-enable Stub Deletion Monitoring at the destination if required J.8 Limitations Junctions / mount points are traversed and copied as expected except as described in . Files deduplicated using the Windows Data Deduplication feature will be copied as expected but each file will be treated as a separate copy. The following are not transferred: symbolic links, other reparse points. K Troubleshooting Before contacting Panzura Support, please review relevant log files and Windows Event Viewer for error messages. K.1 Log Files AdminCenter Logs AdminCenter logs describing each attempted policy operation are accessed through the Recent Tasks panel on the Dashboard. This is the first place to look when investigating a Policy problem. The AdminCenter also maintains a Global Log (accessible from the Help page) which summarizes Policy start / stop activity. For other issues, including failure of user-initiated demigrations, it may be necessary to consult the Agent logs on the servers in question. Server Statistics In addition to log files, AdminCenter also provides per-cluster and per-node charts of operation successes and failures on each Server's Server Details page. This includes information about failed demigrates over time which may be useful in conjunction with a Server's log files to troubleshoot user-initiated demigration issues. Agent Logs Location: Windows: C:\Program Files\Panzura Symphony\logs\Agent Linux: /var/opt/panzura/panzura-symphony-agent/log There are two types of Agent log file. The agent.log contains all Agent messages, including startup, shutdown, and error information, as well as details of each individual file operation (migrate, demigrate, etc.). Use this log to determine which operations have been performed on which files and to check any errors that may have occurred. The messages.log contains a subset of the Agent messages, related to startup, shutdown, critical events and system-wide notifications. Log messages in both logs are prefixed with a timestamp and thread tag. The thread tag (e.g. <A123> ) can be used to distinguish messages from concurrent threads of activity. Log files are regularly rotated to keep the size of individual log files manageable. Old rotations are compressed as gzip (.gz) files, and can be read using many common tools such as 7-zip, WinZip, or zless. To adjust logging parameters, including how much storage to allow for log files before removing old rotations, see link . Log information for operations performed as the result of an AdminCenter Policy will also be available via the web interface. DrTool Logs Location: C:\Program Files\Panzura Symphony\logs\drtool DrTool operations such as recovering files are logged in this location. DrTool will provide the exact name of the log file in the interface. K.2 Interpreting Errors Logged errors are recorded in a tree format which enables user-diagnosis of errors / issues, as well as providing detail for any further investigation by support engineers. Error trees are structured to show WHAT failed, and WHY, at various levels of detail. This section provides a rough guide to extracting the salient features from an error tree. Each numbered line consists of the following fields: WHAT failed &ndash; e.g. a migration operation failed WHY the failure occurred &ndash; e.g. ' [FILE_NOT_FOUND] ' optionally, extra DETAILS about the failure &ndash; e.g. the path to a file As can be seen in the example below, most lines only have a WHAT component, as the reason is further explained by the following line. A Simple Error ERROR demigrate win://server.test/G/source/data.dat [0] ERR_DMAGENT_DEMIGRATE_FAILED [] [] [1] ERR_DMMIGRATESUPPORTWIN_DEMIGRATE_FAILED [] [] [2] ERR_DMAGENT_DEMIGRATEIMP_FAILED [] [] [3] ERR_DMAGENT_COPYDATA_FAILED [] [] [4] ERR_DMSTREAMWIN_WRITE_FAILED [DISK_FULL] [112: There is not enough space on the disk (or a quota has been reached).] To expand the error above into English: demigration failed for the file: win://server.test/G/source/data.dat because copying the data failed because one of the writes failed with a disk full error the full text of the Windows error (112) is provided So, G: drive on server.test is full (or a quota has been reached). Errors with Multiple Branches Some errors result in further action being taken which may itself fail. Errors with multiple branches are used to convey this to the administrator. Consider an error with the following structure: [0] ERR... [1] ERR... [2] ERR... [3] ERR... [4] ERR... [5] ERR... [6] ERR... [3] ERR... [4] ERR... [5] ERR... Whatever ultimately went wrong in line 6 caused the operation in question to fail. However, the function at line 2 chose to take further action following the error &ndash; possibly to recover from the original error or simply to clean up after it. This action also failed, the details of which are given by the additional errors in lines 3, 4 and 5 at the end. Check the Last Line First For many errors, the most salient details are to be found in the last line of the error tree (or the last line of the first branch of the error tree). Consider the following last line: [11] ERR_DMSOCKETUTIL_GETROUNDROBINCONNECTEDSOCKET_FAILED [COULD_NOT_RESOLVE_HOSTNAME] [host was [svr1279.example.com]] It is fairly clear that this error represents a failure to resolve the server hostname svr1279.example.com . As with any other software, the administrator's next steps will include checking the spelling of the DNS name, the server's DNS configuration and whether the hostname is indeed present in DNS. K.3 Contacting Support If an issue cannot be resolved after reviewing the logs, contact Panzura Support at: https://know.panzura.com/ Include the following information in any support request (where possible): Panzura Symphony version A description of the issue &ndash; be sure to include: how long the issue has been present how regularly the issue occurs any changes made to the environment or configuration any specific circumstances which trigger the issue does the issue occur for a particular file and/or server? Operating System(s) Saved system info (.NFO) from msinfo32.exe Source and Destination URIs Applicable Log Files see link for log locations include AdminCenter logs include source agent logs include destination / gateway agent logs remember to include all nodes in each agent cluster zip the entire log folders wherever possible Generate a system configuration file ( support.zip ) from the AdminCenter Help page Any other error messages &ndash; include screenshots if necessary Failure to include all relevant details may delay resolution of your issue. L Glossary ACL - Access Control List; file/folder/share level metadata encapsulating permissions granted to users or other entities. Caretaker - a specific node within a cluster that performs maintenance tasks that must be run on a single node at a time Demigrate - to return migrated file content data to its original location (primary tier), e.g. in response to user access DFS - Microsoft's Distributed File System; comprised of DFSN and DFSR DFSN - DFS Namespace; a Windows mechanism allowing for the presentation of multiple SMB shares as a single logical share DFSR - DFS Replication; an SMB share-based file replication technology, see also Storage Replica as an alternative DR - Disaster Recovery EMA - a REST API providing access to AdminCenter management functions FPolicy - a component of NetApp Data ONTAP which enables extension of native Filer functionality by other applications; Symphony supports both XML and Protobuf external engine formats as appropriate to the ONTAP version FPolicy Server - a server which connects to a NetApp Filer via the FPolicy protocols in order to provide extended functionality FQDN - Fully Qualified Domain Name, e.g. server1.example.com GID - Group ID, e.g. of a UNIX user group GUID - Globally unique identifier HA - High-Availability; specifically the provision of redundant instances of a resource in a manner which ensures availability of service, even in the event of the failure of a particular instance LDM - Link Deletion Monitoring Link-Migrate - to transparently relocate file content data to a secondary storage tier, replacing the original file with a MigLink MigLink - a placeholder for a file that has been Link-Migrated; applications accessing the MigLink will be transparently redirected to the corresponding LinkConnect Server to facilitate data access Migrate - to transparently relocate file content data to a secondary storage tier without removing the file itself; the existing file becomes a stub MWI file - a file on secondary storage which encapsulates the file content data of a corresponding primary storage stub file or MigLink NTP - Network Time Protocol, a protocol for clock synchronization between computer systems over a network Quick-Remigrate - to quickly return a previously demigrated (but unmodified) file back to its migrated state without the need to re-transfer file content data Recovery File - a text file describing the relationships between stubs/MigLinks and their corresponding MWI files Scheduler - the AdminCenter component responsible for starting scheduled Tasks SDM - Stub Deletion Monitoring SID - a Windows Security Identifier SID-History - an Active Directory attribute that maintains the SID history for security principals; Symphony SID History Group Expansion can be enabled to facilitate access to legacy resources following a domain migration Stub - a file whose content data has been transparently migrated to a secondary storage tier location Storage Replica - a Windows Server volume replication technology offering synchronous or asynchronous replication modes Syslog - a protocol used to send system log or event messages, e.g. to a centralized Syslog collector TLS - Transport Layer Security; a protocol used for establishing secure connections between servers (formerly known as SSL) UID - User ID, e.g. of an UNIX user UUID - Universally unique identifier Search results... 2026.1 Go online...
